# 无上玄元三天玉堂大法

**The Supreme Mysterious Primordial Jade Hall of the Three Heavens: A Great Method**

**Scripture Title:** *The Supreme Mysterious Primordial Jade Hall of the Three Heavens: A Great Method*
Compiled by Lu Shizhong of the Song Dynasty. Thirty scrolls.
Source text: *Daoist Canon of the Zhengtong Era*, *Dongzhen* Section, Methods Category.

### **The Supreme Mysterious Primordial Jade Hall of the Three Heavens: A Great Method**
**Scroll One: Elucidating the Great Dao (Chapter One)**

The Master said: The Dao originally has no name, nor does it have form.
The marvel of the Dao is born before Heaven;
Its principle abides after Heaven.
Its teachings were first established in the degenerate age.

For the Dao cannot be sought through form and traces,
Nor can it be attained through sound and color.
All people, from birth, are endowed with this Dao.
Thus, if one’s cultivation and perseverance are steadfast and enduring, ascension may be hoped for.

Yet those unlearned do not awaken to the true essence.
In their daily lives, they are constantly mired in the dust and clamor,
Willingly drowning in the sea of right and wrong, emotions and desires,
Adrift and sinking, unable to extricate themselves.

Thus, the sagely masters, pitying those benighted and unable to comprehend,
Thought it better to guide and lead them forward—hence the rise of teachings and methods.
Though the Daoist methods may not yet enable one to ascend to the True,
They may still be used to seek the True.
Though they may not yet enable one to attain the Dao,
They may still be used to enter the Dao.

Yet sentient beings, unaware of the compassionate intent to guide them,
Assume the Great Dao is merely these teachings and methods.
Thus, they often abandon the true to pursue the false, forsaking the root to chase the branches.
How could they know that the Dao resides within themselves?
If one grasps its essential principles and cultivates them over time, one may attain the True.

Once my true primordial essence is accomplished,
There will be surplus to supplement what is lacking,
And all that is practiced will become the Dao.
If one does not know the secrets of cultivating the True,
But merely engages in the toil of practicing methods,
Receiving unclear instruction and clinging to words on paper,
One drifts ever farther from the Dao.

Thus, the sagely masters’ intent is to first cultivate the self,
And only then can one command ghosts and spirits.
If one does not know that cultivation lies within oneself,
But merely relies on submitting memorials and petitions for retribution,
Or on breath and movement for command,
The heart grows ever more deluded, the effects ever more distant,
One’s true essence daily dissipates, one’s true vitality daily wanes.

Those who inherit these teachings must prioritize enlightenment,
Taking cultivation as the foundation.
How could one then worry about being unable to practice the methods?

The Dao within me can be fully expressed in a single word;
Yet to extend it and transform others cannot be completed in a single word.
Now, the oral instructions of the true masters are set forth below,
So that learners may easily trace the source.
If the Dao is already awakened, then these words are but the trap and snare.
For the unenlightened, one must rely on written expressions—
Thus it is said: "Without scripture, none can be delivered."

The Jade Hall is the natural formation of primordial *qi* into a hall within the Jade Capital Mountain.
Within it dwell the Nine Venerable Elders, born of the *qi* of Radiant Clarity.
The mountain is bathed in golden light, never darkening;
The nine *qi* flourish eternally—this is called the Realm of Jade Purity.
Thus, this teaching emerged from the Jade Capital Mountain, hence the name "Jade Hall."

Yet the marvels of the Jade Capital and the Jasper Hall,
The mystery of the Nine Venerable Primordial Lords,
Far lie in the lofty and luminous heavens,
Near lie within the heavens of one’s own body.

Those who inherit the Jade Hall are companions of Heaven—
And Heaven’s companionship is none other than the Three Luminaries.
Thus, the true masters internally cultivate the Three Luminaries to accomplish the Dao,
And externally employ the Three Luminaries to create talismans.

For the marvel of the Three Luminaries:
Heaven obtains it and endures forever;
Humans follow it and ascend to the True.
Thus, spreading the radiance of the Three Luminaries can cure the world’s illnesses;
Unleashing the dharmic power of the Three Luminaries can command ghosts and spirits;
Proclaiming the majestic virtue of the Three Luminaries can eradicate demonic and numinous disturbances;
Descending the wisdom and illumination of the Three Luminaries can open the netherworld.

Though the methods of the Three Luminaries are simple,
Their practice lies within oneself, boundless and inexhaustible.
Now, learners must unite the Three Luminaries within their bodies
With the Three Luminaries in Heaven.
Only then can one be called a master.

To inherit the teachings, first compare one’s body to Heaven and Earth, aligning the mysterious Dao with the primordial beginning of the original kalpa—this is Heaven’s Great Ultimate. One must then reflect: what is the Great Ultimate within oneself? After Heaven and Earth divided, they took form, just as one’s body does. Knowing that one’s body parallels Heaven and Earth, yet Heaven and Earth endure eternally while the sun and moon revolve, while one’s body is subject to unceasing birth and death—if one wishes to match Heaven’s longevity, one must ponder: by what Dao do Heaven and Earth endure? By what Dao do immortals and transcendents endure? And by what causes does the human body undergo birth and death? When these are comprehended within, the Dao of immortality is attained.

The Master says: The wondrous Dao values emptiness and nothingness; the ancient Dao prioritizes simplicity and plainness. Today’s Dao is neither simple nor plain, nor is it empty and nothing. All elaborate rituals, intricate verses, and recitations—these only distance one further from the Dao in this age. Those who seek the Dao must move from complexity to simplicity, from superficiality to plainness, and from simplicity and plainness ascend to emptiness and nothingness. Only then can one explore the mystery within the mystery.

Purity of mind is called *zhai* (fasting); restraint of the self is called *jie* (precepts). Today, people’s minds are mired in the mundane, and they call eating coarse grains and vegetables *zhai*—this is not merit or virtue, but a misunderstanding. Only by severing all worldly affairs and ceasing to dwell on them can the mind wander with Heaven, the spirit merge with *qi*, and within movement and stillness, creation and transformation fuse as one. Ghosts and spirits respond—this is what is meant by practicing the method.

What does *xingchi* (practice and perseverance) entail? *Xing* means advancing without cease—entering the path of longevity, ascending the gate of true immortality, and enduring without weariness. *Chi* means grasping firmly and enduring, like holding an object in hand, determined not to let it fall. The ancients practiced by first rectifying their own deviations. Today, people practice while their corporeal deviations remain unexpunged, making it easy for external deviations to enter. To seek control over ghosts and spirits thus becomes difficult. If one can maintain a single-minded resolve, in stillness and concentration, responding with the true to the true—this is the subtlety of *xingchi*.

When writing talismans, first enter the chamber, burn incense, and sit in silence for a long while. Once *qi* settles and the spirit is at ease, knock the teeth and circulate the energy, unifying heart and talisman, talisman and heart as one. The eastern radiance requires no turning of the head; the exhalation of *qi* should not produce sound. Grinding ink and applying cinnabar should be as if wielding golden and silver light. When dipping the brush and writing, only luminous clarity should be seen. The circulation of intent should not be sluggish—one stroke reveals all that precedes. The incantation lies in the voice of the heart, precisely when writing the talisman. With a mind unstained by external defilements, write the talisman as if transmitting one’s own spirit. Upon completion, circulate *qi* and bestow the mudra.

For talismans that expel evil, circulate one’s own fierce *qi*; for talismans that deliver and save, circulate the natural, life-giving *qi* of Heaven. The subtlety lies not in outward form but in the secret circulation of *qi*. The use of seals in practice serves to discipline the mind and body. Later generations, lacking understanding, exhaust their minds and bodies. The ancients sealed with the heart; today, people seal with wood. The establishment of ritual seals serves to govern the duties of the method, so that when one holds the seal, there is a place of refuge, and when one impresses it, there is a hierarchy of submission. Those who inherit the teachings must possess the Three Seals—these must not be treated lightly.

Before enlightenment, one relies on wooden seals; after enlightenment, only the seal of the heart remains. Thus it is said: Heaven has its seal, and the Three Luminaries are thereby ordered. Humans have their seal, and the chamber of the spirit is thereby clarified. The seal lies within oneself—why rely on external objects? When no external object is relied upon, it is called *tongxuan* (penetrating the mystery). The mystery within the mystery—this is the subtlety of the Dao.

The method of drawing *qi* lies in the Three Luminaries. To draw the *qi* of the Three Luminaries, one must unite the true with the true. Today, people do not understand the method of drawing *qi*—they merely turn their heads upward, inhale cold *qi*, and exhale warm *qi*. Yet the Three Luminaries in Heaven are exceedingly distant; a single breath cannot truly capture them. Little do they know that one’s own Three Luminaries reside within the body, not far away, requiring no laborious inhalation to naturally endure. The key lies in circulating one’s own true *qi* and gathering it—thus, one need not labor to absorb external *qi*.

The Master says: Unite the heart with the spirit, and the spirit with nothingness. The method of pacing the stars lies in the feet—where the feet tread, the hands also move. As the hands move, the heart also abides. This is what is meant by pacing the *gang* (cosmic pattern). Otherwise, not only will there be no response, but it will also be of no benefit. Those who have attained the Dao, their bodies already pervaded by truth, need not pace to align with the *gang*, nor move to form mudras, nor intentionally abide—yet all abide.

Communion with the true lies in burning incense, and the principle of burning incense is something practitioners must understand. The nature of the Five Phases: fire is said to blaze upward. When paying homage to the true or summoning generals, burning incense uses the sincerity of the heart to borrow the *qi* of fire and ascend. In practice, one must use a blazing fire and abundant incense—one offering reaches its destination. Otherwise, it cannot transcend and ascend.

The format of memorials also has its explanation. The ancients’ hearts communed with Heaven; today, people’s hearts are separated from Heaven. When communing, a single thought and Heaven already knows; when separated, repeated memorials fail to reach Heaven. This is because the mundane heart and the celestial true are cut off from one another. Yet the world relies on paper and ink to write, attempting to convey messages upward through fire—this practice has endured for so long that it has proliferated endlessly, falling into the realm of deliberate action. Those who inherit the teachings today, even if their memorials can reach Heaven, should reduce their number to a minimum, so that the heart may remain in profound stillness, making resonance easier to achieve.

The Master says: The above are the teachings bestowed by the Heavenly Lord, Great Master of the Teachings. Later learners must prioritize cultivation and realization. In the past, when I encountered an immortal master, I received the *Tianxin* method from the ancestral master, seeking oral instructions. Thereupon, the secrets of the Three Luminaries were explained in detail, and the essentials of ascending the hall were transmitted. Thus, I came to know that *Tianxin* pertains to the exorcistic practices of the Jade Hall teachings.

The Master says: The Great Dao requires only lifting one’s eyes to see; the supreme vehicle needs not expend much effort of the heart. It is also said: Close the gate while it is still early; apprehend the thief by knowing the time.

Upon hearing these words, my heart was moved, and I asked again: "When does this occur?"
The Master replied: "The time lies in the Heavenly Heart, like panning for gold in water."

After a long pause, I asked further: "At the beginning of the primordial kalpa of the Original Beginning, who was the ancestral master?"
He said: "Above, there is no further ancestor; only the Dao is the body."
I asked again: "Must there be a surname?"
He did not answer. After a long while, he said: "Not knowing whose child this body is, it precedes the image of the Emperor."

I asked: "What is the appearance of the sacred image?"
The Master said: "Look and you do not see; listen and you do not hear."
I asked: "If it is neither seen nor heard, then there is no Original Beginning?"
The Master said: "Vague and indistinct, yet within it there is something.
Vague indeed, indistinct indeed, yet within it there is an image."

I asked again: "What, after all, is this thing?"
The Master said: "A precious pearl hangs suspended, illuminating the Three Luminaries."

Thereafter, in every question and answer, the discourse was of the most profound mysteries, the subtleties of ascending to perfection. Now, as I preside over the altar to transmit the teachings, the words of the former sagely masters must not be forgotten. Thus, I have gathered these arcane subtleties and recorded them in broad outline. All the Master’s subtle instructions serve to elucidate the essence of the Great Dao. Those who study this will understand that the teachings of the Jade Hall lie in cultivating the mysteries of the Three Luminaries, not in externals—how could they be neglected?

**Tai Shang’s Natural Threefold Ascension Diagram**
*Formula:*
The heart is still, the realm forgotten; alone, guard the Yellow Chamber.
The One True emerges, filling the room with golden light.

*Another formula:*
Silently contain the true, and heaven and earth arrive together.
Motionless and serene, the myriad spirits revere and obey.

*Another formula:*
Close the heart within, the imperial palace far away.
When the yang spirit’s qi is full, step across the golden bridge.

On the night of the Upper Prime in the gengzi year of the Xuanhe era, after offering incense at the star altar and returning to the chamber to preserve the true, an extraordinary fragrance descended. Turning my head, I saw the ancestral master within a radiance of golden light and Brahmanic qi. He said to me: "I am Zhao Sheng of Wu, now serving at the celestial court. In my former life, I dwelt on Mount Tianmu and possessed a secret book. At the time of my ascension, I concealed it atop the Three Mao Peaks of Mount Juqu in Jiangnan. You must go and retrieve it."

Several years later, I was appointed to govern Jinling and made a special pilgrimage to the mountain’s summit. At midnight, divine light spanned the heavens. Digging deep, about three *zhang* down, I found a stone casket containing a silk scroll roughly six or seven *zhang* in length, mixed with fine sand from Penglai. Having obtained it, I arranged it into twenty-four sections to transmit to the world.

In the winter of the bingwu year of the Jingkang era, while residing in Piling, I received a jade decree to transmit this record, permitting the succession of the Dragon-Tiger lineage. The rites of the yang realm and the retributions of the yin realm are thereby made manifest—this surpasses all else. Thus, I know that this Great Teaching is the original vow of the Mysterious Origin and the sagely masters, unlike other methods. For later learners, unless they receive the golden words and purple characters from the divine mouth, they will never be able to wear this teaching.

Later heirs of the teaching, small in attainment, should contemplate the *Natural Ascension Diagram*. Then, they may depart from all talismanic methods. Within a single breath, they can communicate with the true and reach the numinous, subdue demons and vanquish monsters, deliver the dead and rescue the suffering—all these become easy matters. Be reverent, be reverent.

*Recorded by Lu Shizhong, Master of the Three Luminaries of the Great Cavern of Supreme Clarity.*

**End of Scroll One of the Supreme Mysterious Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method**

**Supreme Mysterious Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method**
*Scripture Title:* *Supreme Mysterious Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method*
Compiled by Lu Shizhong of the Song Dynasty. Thirty scrolls.
Source text: *Daoist Canon of the Zhengtong Era*, *Dongzhen* Section, Methods Category.

**Scroll Two of the Supreme Mysterious Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method**
**Chapter Two: The True Master’s Precepts and Disciplines**

The Master says: Precepts and disciplines are the safeguards for beginners.
In high antiquity, there were no precepts, yet one could cultivate the Dao and attain perfection.
In middle antiquity, there were no disciplines, yet one could awaken to the true and realize the Dao.
In later ages, the human heart is drowned by material desires, and innate nature is obscured by false thoughts. Thus, precepts and disciplines arose.

Yet precepts are the most difficult for beginners to uphold. Therefore, the former sages first used disciplines to restrain them. Only after disciplines are not violated can one speak of observing precepts. Now, those who inherit the teaching and aspire to the realm of immortals—how could they fail to observe precepts? Thus, I record the precepts but not the disciplines.

To not see what is desirable keeps the heart from disorder—this still depends on precepts.
But when, though seeing what is desirable, the heart remains undisturbed—what need is there for precepts?

**Three Great Precepts for Ascending the Hall**
**First Precept: Against Lustful Thoughts**
The Master says: In cultivating the Dao, precepts come first.
Lust is easy to preclude; lustful thoughts are difficult to preclude.
To ascend to perfection, first preclude lustful thoughts. When the heart is unmoved, lust will not arise.
Thus, the *Yellow Court Scripture* says: "Immortals and Daoists are not divine; they accumulate essence and amass qi to attain perfection." These are not empty words.

**Second Precept: Against Worldly Thoughts**
The Master says: The toils of the worldly drown the six roots.
The so-called roots can generate branches and leaves. Wherever they touch, they grow, day by day, the branches and leaves multiplying. When the roots of worldly dust are strong and large, one becomes stained by external things—this is called "dust-strength." External things are also called "dust-strength," and external things are also called "consciousness." Where there is consciousness, there is toil—this is called "worldly toil."
Do not cling to the forms of all phenomena. Thus, the *Scripture for Protecting Life* says: "Purify the six roots and sever all demonic obstructions." This is the meaning.

**Third Precept: Against Deluded Intentions**
The Master says: To preclude worldly toil, first preclude deluded intentions.
Where consciousness arises, delusion follows; where intention moves, dust is born.
Thus, in the course of a day, whether deviant or upright, all involve thought. Where thought arises, intention follows—this is deluded intention.
To preclude intention, make the heart like the bright moon at midnight or the limpid waters of an autumn pool—serene and undisturbed. Then delusion will be settled.
Thus, the *Scripture of Purity* says: "Clarify the heart, and the spirit will naturally be clear."

Observe this closely.

The Master says: These three precepts are for those who seek the true and ascend in learning to cultivate and uphold them. For those of the secular world below, who may find it difficult to transcend worldly customs and uphold the great precepts, first impart the *Jade Hall Universal Precepts*, then gradually ascend to the true. The *Jade Hall Universal Precepts* comprise twenty-four articles:

**First Precept: The Heart Does Not Harbor Poison**
The Master says: One must treat all beings—whether friend or foe—with impartiality. Even if anger arises, do not store it in the heart, allowing knots to form and remain unloosed.

**Second Precept: The Eyes Do Not Gaze Upon the Improper**
The Master says: The eyes are servants of form and become stained by what they encounter. When observing, if it is not something one should see, do not look.

**Third Precept: The Tongue Does Not Crave Foulness**
The Master says: Though scholars may not yet permanently abstain from meat and strong flavors, they must not indulge in pungent or repulsive foods.

**Fourth Precept: The Mouth Does Not Utter Improper Speech**
The Master says: Those who study the Dao must quiet speech to nurture qi, and above all, refrain from harsh words, divisive speech, falsehoods, and frivolous talk. Let none of these be violated.

**Fifth Precept: The Ears Do Not Listen to Chaos**
The Master says: All words of right and wrong, as well as perverse and improper matters, are best left unheard.

**Sixth Precept: Wine Does Not Lead to Drunkenness**
The Master says: Wine disrupts the true and corrupts nature; one must not become excessively intoxicated.

**Seventh Precept: Lust Does Not Stir the Passions**
The Master says: Those of lesser attainment may not yet fully abstain, but they must not indulge in base or obsessive desires.

**Eighth Precept: Qi Is Not Used Recklessly**
The Master says: Human qi and blood thrive in stillness and stability; one must not allow the spirit and heart to race wildly.

**Ninth Precept: The Nature Does Not Give Rise to Anger**
The Master says: The nature is inherently tranquil; anger harms it, and when the nature is harmed, the spirit departs. The *True Records* states: "A volatile and violent nature is the thief and sickness of the entire body." Even when anger is unavoidable, constantly reflect on restraining it, and joy will naturally arise.

**Tenth Precept: Against Envy**
The Master says: The human heart, driven by selfish desires, generates envy when others surpass it. Scholars must not allow envy to take root. Let another’s glory be as one’s own.

**Eleventh Precept: Against Jealousy**
The Master says: This is the same as envy.

**Twelfth Precept: Against Greed**
The Master says: Beyond what is needed for clothing and food, all else is superfluous. One must not covet beyond what is sufficient.

**Thirteenth Precept: Against Stinginess**
The Master says: All things beyond the body belong to worldly toil. One should always use them to aid others and never be miserly.

**Fourteenth Precept: Against Arrogance**
The Master says: The Dao resides in humility, modesty, and reverence. When encountering others, always treat them with respect.

**Fifteenth Precept: Against Pride**
The Master says: When favored, think of disgrace; when at ease, contemplate peril. The slightest emergence of pride and falsity damages and depletes one’s fortune and virtue.

**Sixteenth Precept: Against Deceit**
The Master says: Even in the darkness of a room, act as though being observed; never allow deceitful thoughts to arise.

**Seventeenth Precept: Against Flattery**
The Master says: The Dao values truth and uprightness; one must not engage in sycophancy or obsequiousness.

**Eighteenth Precept: Against Licentiousness**
The Master says: Beyond the bounds of propriety and constancy, one must not transgress ritual.

**Nineteenth Precept: Against Desire**
The Master says: If something does not belong to you, do not let desire arise.

**Twentieth Precept: Against Theft**
The Master says: Coveting wealth is theft. One must always refrain from unjust gain, let alone outright theft.

**Twenty-First Precept: Against Pursuing Influence and Contending for Fame**
The Master says: One must not rely on power to intimidate or chase after fame and profit.

**Twenty-Second Precept: Against Indecent Exposure Before the Stars and Improper Worship of Spirits**
The Master says: When relieving oneself day or night, do not face the heavens or turn north. When passing by spirit shrines, do not wander or linger. Entering a temple in such a manner is improper.

**Twenty-Third Precept: Against Killing Living Beings and Destroying Life**
The Master says: Plants possess life; animals possess destiny. Do not kill or destroy them.

**Twenty-Fourth Precept: Against Consuming the Six Pungent Foods**
The Master says: The six pungent foods repel the spirit and qi, disrupting the true origin. They must not be eaten.

The above twenty-four precepts may be upheld by both the secular and the Daoist.

**Rules and Prohibitions for Ascending the Hall**
The Master says: Those who ascend the hall, having already upheld the precepts, must also understand the rules and prohibitions. Without them, the constant teachings and methods will fall into disorder, and the Dharma will not be revered. Thus, those who inherit the teachings must cultivate a nature like jade—warm, lustrous, and flawless.

For those who inherit the teachings: In the presence of the Most High, they are called disciples; in the Three Realms, they are known as true officials. Disciples are called "students of the true," and those who study the true must first cultivate the body. The essence of cultivating the body lies in eliminating selfish desires, refining the spirit, and nurturing the formless to replenish insufficient vitality. Only when vitality is abundant may one seek the Dao of immortality and receive the teachings.

The teachings are not transmitted without the offering of words and the submission of faith; one is not ordained without swearing oaths before heaven and earth. Those who recklessly transmit or receive them will be investigated by the Three Officials and punished by the Four Departments.

When receiving the teachings, one must revere and honor the ordaining master, treating them with the ancient rites due to a father. In this age, some sell the Dharma for profit, treating their ordaining masters with less respect than servants. Those who study the true must remember that the Celestial Master of Han is far beyond reach and cannot be seen. Those who transmit the teachings of the Celestial Master are the ordaining masters—accord them respect, never slighting or belittling them.

When transmitting the teachings and presiding over the altar, overseeing the various Dharma instruments, only those with innate destiny and immortal bones may attain this. If one’s resolve does not remain unwavering from youth to old age, the teachings must not be transmitted. Those who are fickle and insincere must not receive ordination.

When establishing an altar or oratory, choose a place free of graves or cremated remains, not in grand halls or spacious chambers. In bustling cities, select a quiet and broad street. If near a noisy marketplace, ensure the altar is built in a pure location, without needlessly serving the gods. For one who becomes a teacher to humans and heavens, even the spirits and ghosts beneath the earth will submit and serve. If one privately tends to incense and offerings, the Three Officials will investigate and impose penalties.

One should regularly sit upright in an empty chamber, burning incense and silently circulating the qi, so that the Four Controllers descend, the Five Emperors attend at the window, and the immortals and perfected ones draw near. One must constantly study and savor the profound and mysterious, recite and contemplate the teachings, so that the true spirits descend into one’s body. Then the heavenly demons will serve and revere one as a true official, and in the past, one will not be bound by the earthly bureaus but ascend directly to the Upper Palace of Nanchang.

As a teacher of the Three Realms, one must not enter temples for leisure. If unavoidable, one must not flatter or sacrifice to demonic spirits. Instead, one should silently pay homage to the Three Realms, and blessings will naturally follow. Those who violate this will have their transgressions recorded by the Three Officials.

Before being called a teacher, one may only receive the *Ten Scrolls of the Heavenly Heart Orthodox Method of the Ancestral Teachings of One’s Altar*, to assist the true teaching. When one’s merit and conduct become illustrious, one advances to the Seventh Rank of the Jade Hall. Only when the heart remains unwavering does one progress to the Ninth Rank. After advancing through the Ninth Rank without fault, one then receives the *Three Rushing Registers*. Upon receiving all twenty-four ranks in full, one becomes a teacher of humans and heavens.

When performing purification rites and offerings, one is called the *Orthodox One Wondrous Purification*.

**Ranks of the Jade Hall:**
- **First Rank:** Known as *Jade Hall Successor of the Teachings*, one assists the Celestial Master in matters under the Jade Hall.
- **Seventh Rank:** Known as *Jade Hall Successor of the Teachings, True Official*, one serves as the Five Envoys—Eastern Florescence, Southern Culmen, Western Numinosity, Northern Perfection, and Central Yellow—convening affairs of the Three Heavenly Courts.
- **Ninth Rank:** Known as *Jade Hall Successor of the Teachings, True Official*, one serves as the *Great Dharma Master of All Heavens* and the Envoys of Great Clarity, Highest Clarity, and Jade Clarity.
- **Twenty-Fourth Rank:** Known as *Jade Hall Inheriting Teacher*, *Jade Hall Presiding Teacher*, *Jade Hall Perpetual Inheriting Teacher*, and *Jade Hall Grand Master of Teachings*, one then ascends to *Jade Hall Golden Gate Attendant of the Celestial Throne*.

Those above the rank of *Jade Hall Grand Master of Teachings* are all inheriting teachers, bearing titles such as *Perfected of Observant Illumination and Responsive Dao*, *Perfected of Profound Wonder and Empty Clarity*, *Perfected of Cavernous Clarity and True Unity*, and *Perfected of Radiant Vision and Self-Illuminating*. Only after inheriting the teachings for three cycles without fault and attaining a form akin to that of an immortal may one be so addressed.

**Jade Hall Offices:**
- **First Rank:** *Under the Jade Hall of the Celestial Master*.
- **Middle Rank:** *Jade Hall Inheriting Teaching Altar*, *Jade Hall Grand Master of Teachings Altar*.
- **Upper Rank Inheriting Teacher:** *Executive Office of the Supreme Mystery Capital*.

**Petitions:**
- To the *Three Clarities’ Imperial Mysterious Master*, all are memorialized.
- To the *Heavenly Courts of the Upper Realm*, all are reported.
- To the *Five Marchmounts of the Middle and Lower Realms* and below, all are issued writs.
- To village altars and the like, all are sent missives.

*Volume Two of the Supreme Mysterious Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method concludes.*

---

**Volume Three of the Supreme Mysterious Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method**
**Chapter Three: Preserving the True and Cultivating Attainment**

The Master said: The human heart is deluded and confused, submerged in passions and desires, clinging to dusty realms and ceaselessly pursuing them, like a traveler lost on a desolate road, unaware of where to return. Thus, this method is established to gather the wandering mind. In this way, the heart of desire gradually departs, and the true origin may return. Only then can one ride the void and command qi, exiting the manifest and entering the unmanifest.

Yet once the true origin has returned, the Dao is near to me—why go to such lengths?
The Master said: Sight and hearing leak the qi of the original spirit. Thought and worry scatter the essence of the original yang. Cravings deplete the spirit of the original harmony. Those who study the higher path, in moments of leisure, should silently gather their vision and return their hearing, contain the true within and inwardly observe, restrain desires and moderate emotions—then the immortal Dao is near.

**Daily Absorption of the Three Lights’ Upright Qi**
The Master said: Each day at dawn, face the sacred direction and offer incense, absorbing the qi according to the method—this is most wondrous. If sitting calmly without distractions, in a quiet chamber with a settled mind, one may perform this with eyes half-closed. "Half-closed" means not fully shutting the eyes.

The Master said: Press the left thumb against the upper joint of the middle finger to form the *Sun Lord Mudra*, recite the *Sun Lord Mantra* nine times, hold the mudra before the heart, and inhale the sun’s qi through the nose. Visualize the sun’s five colors entering the five viscera, then swallow the qi along with it.

Next, change to the *Moon Lord Mudra* by pressing the left thumb against the upper joint of the fourth finger, recite the *Moon Lord Mantra* nine times, hold the mudra before the heart, and inhale the moon’s qi through the nose. Visualize its five colors entering the five viscera, then swallow the qi along with it.

Next, press the left thumb against the base of the second finger’s nail to form the *Celestial Stem Mudra*, recite the *Celestial Stem Mantra* seven times, place both hands on the knees, tilt the head back, and visualize the Great Crimson Heaven, from which the Celestial Stem hangs with ten thousand *zhang* of fiery light, fine as silk, crackling with sound. Draw it fully into the mouth, and if any light remains, let it cover the body. Then swallow the qi and store it in the cinnabar field.

**Morning Audience at the Jade Hall to Greet the Original Qi**
The Master said: When a student of the true has matters to report, one should enter the chamber, sit upright, and visualize oneself as a sphere of true qi, radiant as the bright moon. Within this light, see the Golden Gate within the Mysterious Capital Mountain, where there is a White Jade Hall, and the Elder Lord within. Ascend the hall and pay homage.

The incantation says:
*Concluded, see the Elder Lord between the brows, light dividing into sun and moon, illuminating me. I inhale it into my mouth, visualize golden light enveloping my body. Heaven is clear, earth is level, sun and moon shine bright. I ride the original qi, ascend to greet the Heavenly Lord. The Heavenly Lord bestows upon me a body of light. The original qi of the Mysterious Origin eternally preserves my long life.*

Another incantation says:
*Concluded, swallow the saliva and withdraw.*

The Master said: Practicing this regularly, whenever one has matters to report, the inner and outer will align, and one will communicate with the true and summon the numinous.

*On auspicious days of original yang, pay homage at the Jade Hall. Sun and moon bathe me, refining my soul and spirit. Three thousand hairs, twelve thousand radiant essences. United with the Dao in truth, refining my golden chamber. Gathered within me, equal in length to heaven.*

**Restraining the Corpse-Spirits and Seven Po**

The Master said: When yang wanes and yin waxes in a person, when desires and passions deplete the original essence, it is always because the Three Corpses and Seven Po disturb and disrupt the celestial truth. On every *gengshen*, *jiazi*, one’s own birthday, and the evenings of the fifth, thirteenth, and twenty-third days of each month, the three hun-souls become unsettled—*Shuangling*, *Taiguang*, and *Youjing* drift and wander, their radiance scattering, their forms dissolving. The hidden essence stirs in chaos, and all three hun-souls abandon the body, roaming the bedchamber or becoming ensnared by external malevolence, seized by ghosts and spirits, unable to return. Far from their corporeal form, the two qi engage in strife, drying and scorching the inner child, giving rise to illness and disordering the true origin—all stems from this. Those who cultivate the truth must, on these days, restrain and retain them to prevent their escape.

The method of restraint: lie down in repose, stretch the feet, cross the hands over the heart, close the eyes, and hold the breath for three cycles. Then, knock the teeth three times. Visualize a red qi, the size of a chicken’s egg, rising from within and emerging through the mouth. Let the red qi enter the left and right eyes, then exit again. Expand the red qi until it envelops the body above and below, transforming into fire that burns through the self, inside and out, until a faint warmth is felt. Knock the teeth three more times and call the names of the hun-souls: *Shuangling*, *Taiguang*, *Youjing*. Recite the incantation:

*Within the Mysterious Palace of the Great Tenuity,
The Primordial Yellow and First Green.
Refine the three hun within,
Let Taiguang be at peace.
The divine chamber, the Jade Hall,
Born with me as one.
Do not stir recklessly,
Watched over by the Great Numinous.
If you wish to fly and wander,
Go only to the Upper Clarity.
If you hunger or thirst,
Drink the Mysterious Water and Jade Essence.*

Another incantation says:
*Hold the breath.*

Within the Mud-Pill Palace, sun and moon shine brightly. Sleep in stillness. Practice this regularly, and yang will flourish while yin wanes. The Corpse-Spirits will be restrained, the hun-souls and spirits will be strong and at peace. No illness will invade—this is the ladder to seeking immortality.

*Great Spirit of Taiguang,
Celestial Lord of the Imperial Net.
Holding the embryonic talisman,
Wearing a purple crown.
Yellow revolves, red essence,
Ascends to the Gate of Life,
Transforms the spirit, returns to life.*

The Master said: On the new moon, full moon, and last day of each month, the Seven Po roam and consort with ghosts and demons, wasting and toying with the original yang. They often cause people to be erratic in joy and anger, unstable in sorrow and worry, indulgent in lust and pleasure, constantly deluded and confused, creating the roots of illness and obstructing progress on the Dao. The method to restrain the Po: on those evenings, lie down in repose and stretch the feet. Cover the ears with both hands, interlocking the fingers atop the head. Hold the breath seven times. Visualize a white radiance at the tip of the nose, the size of a small bean, gradually expanding until it crowns the body in nine layers. After a long while, it transforms into two blue-green dragons within the eyes, white tigers in the nostrils, a vermilion bird in the heart, and a tortoise and serpent beneath the feet. Two jade maidens, clad in brocade, hold flames before the ear gates. Swallow the saliva seven times and call the names of the Seven Po: *Shigou*, *Fushi*, *Queyin*, *Tunzei*, *Feidu*, *Chuhui*, *Choufei*. Recite the incantation:

*Visualize the sun in the heart,
The moon in the kidneys.
The two qi intertwine their light,
Forming an infant to guard the cinnabar field.
Nine layers of plain qi,
Restrain the Po and govern their release.
Celestial beasts guard the gates,
Jade maidens hold the passes.
Refine the Po to harmony and softness,
Let them be at peace with me.
Do not stir recklessly,
Observe and examine the source of form.
If you hunger or thirst,
Drink the sun’s yellow and the moon’s cinnabar.*

Another incantation says:
*Ingest the Heavenly Sovereign’s Life-Preserving Talisman in peace.*

The true qi lingers,
The nine portals shine open.
The Corpse-Spirits and Po are restrained,
Forbidden to come and go.
Refine yang and exchange qi,
Guard the numinous terrace in haste.
External malevolence cannot intrude,
The inner truth returns of itself.
Gathered and undispersed,
The yang radiance returns to the womb.

**Heavenly Sovereign’s Life-Preserving Talisman**
Write in cinnabar on yellow paper, face east, and ingest.

The Master says: Those who study immortality must pacify the mind and nurture the spirit, ingesting and refining to cure illness, filling the brain palace to its fullness so that the primordial essence does not tilt. Only then may one preserve the spirit and practice the breathing of the Two Radiant Ones. If one frequently engages in sexual union, the qi becomes defiled and the spirit flees, essence withers and the body is exhausted. Thus, true immortals first abstain from lust. If one does not abstain or restrain oneself, even with diligent practice, one cannot replenish the depletion—this is merely lending qi to a moving corpse. If you can abstain from excess and purify the heart, then practicing this method may lead you into the wondrous subtleties of the High Ascent.

The *Supreme Mysterious Primordial Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method*, Scroll Three, ends here.

---

**Supreme Mysterious Primordial Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method**
*Scripture Title:* *Supreme Mysterious Primordial Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method*
Compiled by Lu Shizhong of the Song Dynasty. Thirty scrolls.
Source of the base text: *Daoist Canon*, *Methods* section of the *Dongzhen* division.

**Supreme Mysterious Primordial Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method, Scroll Four**
**Chapter Four: The Inner Realm of the High Ascent**

The Master says: Those who study the supreme Dao and aspire to immortality must rely on the essence of the sun and the radiance of the moon to refine and complete the immortal way. Without the mysterious practice, none can unite with the real. This so-called "essence and radiance" is not sought from without but is the true attainment of one’s own body. Daoist methods have a thousand gates and ten thousand doors, winding paths and side trails, with杂说纷繁冗杂. Thus, many learners abandon the real for the false, forsake the internal for the external. The longer they practice, the harder it is to achieve success. Now, the High Ascent of the sun and moon is the wondrous teaching transmitted by the Most High to the ancestral masters of later times. In ancient times, it was passed down only orally, without reliance on written words. Now, it is specially recorded in writing so that those of later generations with karmic affinity may easily seek and investigate it. Thus, the *Huangting [Neijing]* states: "In the High Ascent of the sun and moon, I ascend the Dao; Yu Yi and Jie Lin guard me well." This is what it means.

The name of the sun’s *hun* is the Jade Emperor, with the jade taboo-name.
The Five Emperors wear robes of five-colored brocade and jade capes, with flying feather skirts and lotus crowns.

Within the sun:
- The Green Emperor’s taboo-name is *Yuán Cháng Yuán*, his style *Zhào Lóng Tāo*.
- The Red Emperor’s taboo-name is *Dān Líng Zhì*, his style *Lǜ Hóng Yìng*.
- The White Emperor’s taboo-name is *Hào Yù Jiāng*, his style *Huí Jīn Xiá*.
- The Black Emperor’s taboo-name is *Chéng Zēng Tíng*, his style *Xuán Lǜ Yán*.
- The Yellow Emperor’s taboo-name is *Shòu Yì Fù*, his style *Biāo Huī Xiàng*.

The names of the inner spirits of the Five Emperors’ *hun* essence are *Zhū Jǐng*, their style *Chì Tóng Chì Qì*.

The Supreme Dao Lord’s taboo-name is *Jiāng Jūn*, his style *Gāo Qiān Shuǎng*.

The name of the moon’s *pò* is the Five August Ladies, with the jade taboo-name.
The Ladies all wear three-cornered buns with hair hanging to the shoulders, robes of five-colored brocade capes, and dragon-phoenix flying feather skirts.

Within the moon:
- The Green August Lady’s taboo-name is *Yǐn É*, her style *Fēn Yīng Yàn*.
- The Red Qi August Lady’s taboo-name is *Yì Yì Liáo Wú*, her style *Wǎn Yán Xū*.
- The White August Lady’s taboo-name is *Líng Sù Lán*, her style *Yù Lián Huá*.
- The Black August Lady’s taboo-name is *Jié Lián Qiáo*, her style *Chún Lì Jīn*.
- The Yellow August Lady’s taboo-name is *Qīng Yíng Jīn*, her style *Gèn Dìng Róng*.

The Supreme Dao Mother of the moon’s yellow qi has the taboo-name *Dào Yào Zhī*, her style *Zhèng Huì*, and is titled *Tiáo Fūren*.

The name of the inner spirit of the *hun* essence is *Ài Xiāo*, its style *Tái Biāo*.

The Master says: The taboo-names of the sun and moon’s *hun* are most secret. The Most High concealed the names of the sun and moon in the Purple Terrace Jade Palace; those who know them communicate with the spirits. At dawn on the first day of the lunar month, sit upright, purify the fast, and settle the mind. Knock the teeth thirty-six times. First visualize one’s own cinnabar field as a great sea, with the sun rising from the sea. One’s own body sits atop the crown of the head, the body like a mountain of stone.

Recite the incantation:
*"Yang arises from the primordial sea,
Rising from below.
The chaotic yang essence
Dispels the host of yin.
Within is a great spirit,
The Lord Yu Yi.
Descend with this true qi,
Bathe my form."*

After reciting the incantation, swallow the saliva nine times. Next, visualize the sun ascending in golden light, illuminating and reflecting one’s true form, which ascends to the sun palace.

*"The golden pivot radiates auspiciousness,
Pervading the brilliance of yang.
The flaming light soars and flies,
Flowing essence for ten thousand miles.
Demon vapors extinguish their flames,
Dust and filth are swept clean.
Soaring through emptiness, stepping on qi,
I ride the qi to ascend on high."*

After reciting the incantation, swallow the saliva nine times. Next, ride the fire dragon to rush to the sun palace. The fire dragon leads the way, piercing the crown with flying light. The spirit enters the realm of nothingness, paying homage to Yu Yi. In the blink of an eye, ascend and merge with the numinous radiance. The one true follows its origin, burning away the corpse of Peng.

After reciting the incantation, swallow the saliva nine times, and contemplate entering the sun palace, the entire body becoming one. After a long while, forget the form, melting like spring. Practicing this for one year dispels illness, commands ghosts and spirits, and comes and goes naturally. After two years, one communicates with immortals and receives the attendance of the Three Realms. After three years, the Demon King vouches for one. After nine years, the practice is complete, and the Five Emperors befriend one. A decree is issued to appoint one as a Perfected, and one attains longevity.

The Master says: Once the student has practiced the Way of Rushing to the Sun, next visualize oneself as Mount Kunlun, sitting atop the mountain’s peak, with a great sea below and the moon’s wheel newly risen. Swallow the saliva three times and knock the teeth three times.

Recite the incantation:

The true radiance first arises, the utmost yang within yin. Water overflows the mysterious wheel, golden dew emits a faint glow. The source of saliva flows freely, its brilliance illuminating the jade chamber. Qi grows in luminous abundance, and one’s service enables flight.

Incantation:
*(Incantation concluded, swallow saliva nine times.)*

Next, visualize the moonlight as a half-crescent, its golden light shining upon one’s body. The radiance disperses into the Celestial Pond, gold and water forming a half-crescent. The light illumines the dark night, shining upon my mysterious pearl. Drinking the crystalline nectar, its fragrance permeates the numinous body. After several cycles of true convergence, one rides the radiance in soaring flight.

Incantation:
*(Incantation concluded, swallow saliva nine times, knock the teeth, and visualize the moon as full. True water forms a bridge, descending to connect with the mountain’s stone. My body, riding a multicolored phoenix, enters the moon. The celestial source circulates, its light penetrating the layered towers. The night sky reflects in all directions, the five fluids stirring the depths. Soaring through emptiness, one captures the radiance, and the true body floats in flight. With a single ascent to the true, the nine yangs hold no peril.)*

*(Recitation concluded, swallow saliva nine times, and visualize entering the Lunar Palace, becoming one with the body. After a long while, forget the form, sensing the golden light teaching in all four directions, illuminating the entire sky. Practicing this for one year dispels illness, commands ghosts and spirits, and comes and goes naturally. After two years, one communicates with Perfected Ones, and the Three Realms attend. After three years, the Demon King vouches for one. After nine years, the Five Ladies issue a decree, and one’s form attains flight as an immortal.)*

The Master says: The mystery of the two radiances is not something lesser scholars can comprehend. Those who understand it should practice diligently, and their bodies will emit light, befriending the myriad Perfected Ones. They will attain the Dao and become Perfected, eventually ranking among the Flying Immortals of the sun and moon, their longevity matching heaven and earth, their flight unbounded. This is a secret of the highest immortals—guard it well, guard it well.

*End of Scroll Four of the Supreme Mystery-Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method*

---

**Scroll Five of the Supreme Mystery-Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method**
**Chapter Five: Ascending the Dipper and Rushing to the Stars**

The Master says: For protecting the body and prolonging life, nothing surpasses the Dipper’s true essence in restraining the hun-soul and refining yang. Thus, the sages say: "Entering and exiting within the Dipper, the body grows strong and qi flourishes, extending years and increasing destiny—all evil shuns one." They also say: "All methods emerge from the Dipper, and all spirits are commanded by the Dipper." Thus, every method and practice cannot connect with the true or respond to the numinous without the Dipper’s truth. Therefore, the sagely masters necessarily teach ascending the Dipper and pacing the stars, hoping that students may communicate with immortals, attain the true, preserve the origin, and guard existence.

The essence of the Great Star is named the Mysterious Pivot Spirit, called the Yang Brightness Hun, or the Celestial Pivot Hun. Its spirit ascends as the Celestial Grand Commandant, governing the correction of transgressions. Above, it oversees the Nine Heavens; in the middle, it supervises the Five Peaks’ Flying Immortals; below, it commands those who study immortality, as well as the spirits of heaven and earth.

The essence of the Origin Star is named the Northern Terrace Spirit, called the Yin Essence Hun, or the Celestial Rotator Hun. Its spirit is the Dipper Heaven’s Grand Steward, governing rank and emolument. Above, it oversees the celestial lodges; below, it commands the myriad spirits and those who study immortality.

The essence of the True Star is named the Nine Ultimates Supreme Perfected Spirit, called the Perfected Person Hun, or the Celestial Mechanism Hun. Its spirit is the Dipper Heaven’s Minister of Works, governing immortals. Above, it oversees the Nine Heavens’ lofty Perfected Ones; in the middle, it supervises the Five Peaks’ numinous immortals.

The essence of the Pivot Star is named the Mysterious Root Spirit, called the Dark Obscurity Hun, or the Celestial Balance Po. Its spirit is the Dipper Heaven’s Mobile Strike General, governing the punishment of rebels. Above, it oversees the Nine Heavens’ ghosts and spirits; in the middle, it commands the Northern Emperor’s Three Officials; below, it monitors the myriad multitudes.

The essence of the Mainstay Star is named the Great Peace Spirit, called the Cinnabar Origin Hun, or the Jade Balance Po. Its spirit is the Dipper Heaven’s Dipper Lord, governing life records. Above, it oversees the Nine Heavens’ registers; in the middle, it governs the ghosts and spirits’ ledgers; below, it commands those who study the true.

The essence of the Chronicle Star is named the Life Mechanism Spirit, called the Northern Culmen Hun, or the Open Yang Po. Its spirit is the Dipper Heaven’s Grand Master of Ceremonies, governing advancement. Above, it oversees the Nine Heavens’ Supreme Perfected Ones; in the middle, it supervises the Five Peaks’ Flying Immortals.

The essence of the Pass Star is named the Origin Yang Spirit, called the Celestial Pass Hun, or the Shaking Dipper Great Brightness. It governs the Supreme Emperor of Heaven, controlling the mechanisms of heaven and earth’s fortune and misfortune.

The spirit of the August Jade Emperor is called the Eight Radiances Void Origin Lord. The spirit of the Great Tenuity Jade Emperor Lord is called the Seven Essences Seven Spirit Lords. Those who behold these two stars attain longevity; those who cultivate them become immortals.

The Master says: Regularly on the twenty-first night of the month, enter the chamber at midnight, connect with the settled qi, close the eyes, and inwardly gaze. Then, one’s entire body slowly rises, flying upward into the Dipper’s bowl, sitting with one’s back to the Perfected One. After a long while, one senses one’s body within the Dipper. Exerting utmost effort, one feels heat within the body—this is the true qi harmonizing with virtue. Visualize the Dipper’s purple light descending upon one’s body, illuminating both inside and out. Once one has arrived within the Dipper, sit with one’s back to the Perfected One. Then, proceed to pay homage to each star, reciting the prayer:

To the first, the Great Star’s essence, the Mysterious Pivot Supreme Perfected: May I attain flight as an immortal, riding the void and steering the floating.
To the second, the Origin Star’s essence, the Northern Terrace Supreme Perfected: May I attain flight as an immortal, roaming the Jasper Terrace.
To the third, the True Star’s essence, the Nine Ultimates Supreme Perfected: May I attain flight as an immortal, governing the Three Mysteries.
To the fourth, the Pivot Star’s essence, the Mysterious Root Supreme Perfected: May my jade name be listed among the Flying Immortals.
To the fifth, the Mainstay Star’s essence, the Great Peace Supreme Perfected: May I attain flight as an immortal, ascending to Highest Clarity.
To the sixth, the Chronicle Star’s essence, the Life Mechanism Supreme Perfected: May I attain flight as an immortal, my name inscribed in the Great Tenuity.
To the seventh, the Pass Star’s essence, the Origin Yang Supreme Perfected: May I attain flight as an immortal, commanding the Jade Lads.
To the eighth, the August Star’s essence, the Highest Jade Emperor Lord: May I attain flight as an immortal, ascending the Hall of the Latter Sage.
To the ninth, the Venerable Star’s essence, the Great Tenuity Jade Emperor Lord: May I attain flight as an immortal, entering the cinnabar chamber and jade palace.

Once the invocation is complete, visualize the qi of the Dipper in its black, yellow, red, and purple hues descending to infuse your divine body, merging with these same colored qi as they flow downward into the Cavern Chamber. The incantation reads:

*"Primordial essence of the Cavern Chamber,
Supreme Infant of the Crimson One.
The Dipper’s radiant canopy
comes to illumine the Muddy Pellet.
Refine and guard my bones and blood,
restrain and govern my poised and hun souls.
May I ascend as an immortal,
riding clouds to greet the dawn.
Pay homage to the Jade Emperor,
to the Supreme Unity, the Primordial Sovereign."*

When the incantation is finished, close your eyes, still your thoughts, and forget the form to rest in tranquil sleep. Next, visualize yourself at the Dipper’s mouth, drawing in the black, yellow, red, and purple qi to enter your mortal body.

**Chapter Six of the Supreme Mystery’s Demon-Quelling Canon**
The Master said: The Most High cherishes life and does not display might to enforce punitive decrees. Yet when demonic spirits grow frenzied, when malevolent gods transform and shift, harming people and creatures, mocking the true Dao—then, as a last resort, the ultimate statutes of restraint are established.

For the adept, cultivation and realization must come first. Once one attains the subtleties of the real, ghosts and spirits will rise in reverence, the Three Realms will submit in devotion—how could one then rely on awe and severity to govern?

The Master said: Before the first kalpa unfolded and heaven and earth first took shape, primordial qi circulated, and people lived in benevolence and longevity. But as yin waned and yang dissipated, ghosts and spirits gradually arose. From the celestial winds above to the springs and soil below, they manifested in myriad forms across all directions, all born of wayward qi in creation, inheriting the baleful shapes of heaven and earth. They spread poison and practice perversity, acting as their nature dictates.

Thus, even the stellar palaces have their ghosts, capable of causing disasters. Heaven and earth, too, have their ghosts, who oversee human fortune and misfortune. The sixty cyclical days each have a deity presiding over them. Their retinues include thousands of ghosts and ten thousand demons, flying through the world. Heaven can give them life but cannot entirely extinguish them—hence this method is used to govern them.

Yet this canon represents the ultimate punishment of the heavens and must not be employed lightly.

**Register of Ghosts and Demons**
The Ten-Thousand-Zhang Ghost of High Heaven, king of the hundred common ghosts, surnamed Xi, celestial name Six Directions, dwells in the waters southeast of Mount Tai.

The Three Elders of the Southern Village, lords of the Daoist dead, surnamed Che, named Ni, reside northwest of Mount Tai. They oversee the ledgers of the dead, examine the sins of the living, command official subordinates, and can also harm people.

The Executioner Ghost of the Northern Dipper, clad in black above and below, seven thousand zhang in height, surnamed Wu, named Huan.

The Executioner Ghost of the Dipper’s Web at Midnight, nine zhang tall, dressed in red, nameless, responsible for slaying traitors and rebels across the world.

The Executioner Ghost of the Supreme Unity, formless and nameless, one zhang and six feet tall, clad in red.

The Celestial Three-Five Executioner Ghost, named Gui, one zhang and seven feet tall, dressed in white with a red headband, wielding a halberd.

The Great Ghost of the Northern Dipper’s Three Terraces, surnamed Ban, named Wan.

The Ghost of the Western Dipper’s Three Terraces, surnamed Zhuo, named Qiu.

The Ghost of the Southern Dipper’s Three Terraces, surnamed Ming, named Wen.

The Ghost of the Eastern Dipper’s Three Terraces, surnamed Jiao, named Che.

The Ghost of the Central Dipper’s Three Terraces, surnamed Wang, named Xian.

The five Dipper ghosts above record human transgressions and often bring calamity and slaughter upon people.

The Master of the Five Dipper’s Reversed Executioner Ghosts, named Xu.

The Ghost of the Five Directions’ Direct Talisman, named Jie Tian.

The Celestial One’s Long-Harming Descendants Ghost, named Gao Bi.

The Celestial Flying Long-Ensnaring Ghost, named Liang Tian.

The above ghosts are regularly dispatched by the Three Officials and the Northern Emperor to investigate human sins, and they constantly dwell among people. These are called Celestial Demons. Each initially took form from the qi of heaven and earth’s yin and yang, unlike lesser specters. To offend them brings great harm. They may be restrained by talismans but should not be killed.

**The Heavenly Emperor’s Talisman for Restraining Celestial Demons**
The talisman employs the Jade Clarity mudra on yellow silk. Worn or displayed, it ensures peace and auspiciousness.

The Master said: Long ago, the High Perfected of the Supreme Ultimate, the Wenchang Lord of the Dao, rode a cloud-dragon treasure chariot, a jade carriage with wheel-rims of nephrite, its canopy tilted and axle turned, ascending the sacred Mount Emei. There, he saw the people of the lower realms oppressed by various demons and ghosts. The ghosts were numerous, their names diverse, roaming the world and slaughtering the innocent. Thus, he established the method for slaying ghosts and restraining demons to govern them. One who knows a ghost’s name will never suffer its harm; calling its name three times, the ghost will perish of itself.

Jiazi: Yuan Guang.
Yichou: Bing Zhang.

Here follows the translation:

---

The sixty ghost names listed above belong to spirits with human bodies, red fur, no clothing, ears but no eyes, capable of flying a thousand *li*. Their forms span three *zhang*, and they bring harm to the imperial subjects. Knowing their names, ghosts dare not approach. Calling their names thrice, they weep and flee a thousand *li*. There are talismans to subdue and control them.

To subdue the **Great Year Ghost Generals of Yin-Yang of the Jiazi Era**, the talisman is a celestial secret, guarded by three thousand **Heavenly Ding Soldiers of the Three Heavens** and sixty-four **Jade Maidens**. To restrain and subdue them, one must inscribe the **Great Slayer Text** in black on yellow paper and make a petition—greatly auspicious.

**Worldly Ghost Names:**
- **Mountain Spirit:** Zhuo Nei
- **Wood Spirit:** Qun Yao
- **Stone Spirit:** Pi
- **Monkey Spirit:** Ma Li Ze Hao
- **Celestial Tree:** Fang Yu
- **Fox Spirit:** Jia Fa Gan
- **Great Mountain:** Gong Qiang
- **Lesser Mountain:** He Bing
- **Brick and Stone:** Yue Su
- **Pomegranate Wood:** Xia Tuo
- **Ghost Lust:** Zai Zhi
- **Woman Lust:** Jie Jiao
- **Blue Qi:** Wen Gao Yuan
- **White Qi:** Wen Bo Lai
- **Red Qi:** Wen Shi Xuan
- **Black Qi:** Wen Wen Duan
- **Yellow Qi:** Wen Jun Tai
- **House and Chamber:** Yao Zi
- **Qi-Eater:** Hou Fu
- **Latrine:** Xiang Fu
- **Well:** Rong Qiong Jiu
- **Kitchen Hearth:** Gui Rang Gan
- **Bed and Couch:** He Zi
- **Umbrella and Canopy:** Yan
- **Banner and Pennant:** Tuo
- **Sound of Peng:** Luan
- **Sheng and Reed Pipes:** Gou
- **Halberd:** Yi Er Qin
- **Sword and Blade:** Zi Fu
- **Armor:** Zi Xian
- **Millennial White Bones:** Yuan Shi
- **Centennial White Bones:** Yin Chu
- **River Earl:** Da
- **Four Waterways:** Hou
- **Three Rivers:** Jian
- **Iron Spirit:** Ming Yi Yuan
- **Metal Spirit:** Ming Yi Chong
- **Bronze Vessel Ghost:** Yang Sha
- **Pillar Wood:** Wen Luo
- **Clothing and Garments:** Shi Lian
- **Five Colors:** Ti Jing
- **Tomb Earl:** Gong Xia Hou
- **Tomb Ghosts:** Two Thousand Later

All these ghosts traverse the world, relying on forms and borrowing natures. In spring, their legions number in the millions, roaming and blocking the four directions, filling the six harmonies. The **Most High** possesses methods to restrain them—they dare not stir, fleeing at the sound of their names and scattering at the sight of talismans.

**Northern Emperor’s Fire Bell Toss to Annihilate Demons and Slay Ghosts—Supreme Talisman**

**Incantation:**
*The Northern Emperor commands, burning the ghost camps.*
*Slaying demon ghosts, severing evil spirits.*
*The Heavenly Ding soldiers advance boldly, casting fire and ringing bells.*
*Foul smoke billows, crimson flames blaze bright.*
*The Three Realms are pacified, all forms destroyed for ten thousand li.*
*Those who dare disobey are swiftly sent to the Dark City.*
*Bound by wind blades, eternally sunk in the Nine Ramparts.*
*No pardon is granted—execute upon talisman’s arrival.*
*Hasten to obey the Northern Emperor’s decree!*

**Three Heavens Demon-Slaying Jade Script**　**True Emperor’s Spirit**

The above **Ghost-Slaying Talisman** is inscribed in cinnabar on red paper. To subdue demons and slay ghosts, address the **Ghost-Slaying Demon-Restraining Generals and Scribes**, burning the petition in the central courtyard. That night, black winds and fierce rains will arise, and the ghosts will perish of themselves. If there is wind without rain, the ghosts flee a thousand *li*. If there is neither wind nor rain, the entity is no great demon or evil spirit, and the celestial authorities will not execute the extreme penalty. Take note—this must not be taken lightly.

Once the retribution is complete, inscribe the **Jade Script** in cinnabar on yellow paper, or on *xiang* wood, to permanently secure the land. Welcome the **qi of life and prosperity**, ensuring no further demonic afflictions.

**The Fifth Scroll of the Supreme Mystery, Primordial Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method** concludes here.

---

**Supreme Mystery, Primordial Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method**
**Scripture Title:** *Supreme Mystery, Primordial Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method*
Compiled by Lu Shizhong of the Song Dynasty. Thirty scrolls.
Source text: *Daoist Canon of the Zhengtong Era*, **Methods Category of the Dongzhen Section**.

**Sixth Scroll of the Supreme Mystery, Primordial Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method**
**Chapter Seven: Altar Rituals and Dignified Conduct**

The Master said: Solemnity, reverence, secrecy, and harmony—these are the affairs of inner truth. Banners, pennants, standards, and their measured movements—these are the affairs of outer ritual. Yet when sincerity unites with truth and application is seamless, one becomes a companion to Heaven and Earth. Even so, outer ritual is still required to discipline the realm.

In every bow and rise, every advance and retreat, all that the eye sees and the ear hears must be proper. With no opening for wayward thoughts, one may communicate with Heaven and truly reach the **Supreme Emperor**. Thus it is said: *Model Heaven, emulate Earth, and imitate the world’s dignified conduct*—then all actions will be solemn and respectful.

For altar and meditation rites, the structure has three tiers, reflecting the distinction between the **Heavenly Honored** and the lowly earth. On the altar’s upper tier stands the **Vacuous August**, the **Celestial Treasure Flower Terrace of the Jade Capital Mountain**, where the **Three Treasures and Imperial Masters** are enshrined. To the left, the **Banner of the Heavenly-Appointed Demon-Subduing** is erected; to the right, the **Standard of the Lion and Evil-Expelling**. On the left of the left, the **Talisman for Communicating with Truth** is placed to descend the thousand truths. On the right of the right, the **Talisman for Reaching the Spirits** is set to summon the ten thousand spirits. In the center, the **Three Dawn Talismans** are displayed to connect with the myriad *qi* and dispel demonic miasmas.

To the east of the altar, plant the **Blue Dragon Banner Talisman**; to the west, the **White Tiger Banner Talisman**; to the south, the **Vermilion Bird Banner Talisman**; to the north, the **Dark Warrior Banner Talisman**. In the five directions, arrange the **Jade Talismans for Pacification and Stabilization**—this constitutes the uppermost tier.

If three tiers are not used, arrange them according to the directions within the hall or palace. If ascending three tiers, the middle tier is set with eight gates:
- **Northwest:** **Cloud Jade Vacuity Truth-Communicating Gate**
- **Due North:** **Clear and Cold Mysterious Unity Gate**
- **Northeast:** **Tranquil and Natural Gate**
- **Due East:** **Azure Florescence Beginning Gate**
- **Southeast:** **Pure Harmony and Rigorous Yang Gate**
- **Due South:** **Pure Yang Blaze and Radiance Gate**
- **Southwest:** **Earth Compliance and Metal Harmony Gate**
- **Due West:** **Rigorous Brightness and Luminous Splendor Gate**

On the lower tier, the twelve *qi* are arrayed:
- **Zi Position:** **Dark Heaven’s Dense Beginning Qi**
- **Chou Position:** **Northern Origin’s Natural Qi**
- **Yin Position:** **Evil-Expelling and Demon-Dispelling Qi**
- **Mao Position:** **Beginning Azure and Flourishing Origin Qi**
- **Chen Position:** **Yellow Spirit’s Lofty Mystery Qi**
- **Si Position:** **Tranquil Spirit’s Serene Quiet Qi**
- **Wu Position:** **Fiery Truth’s Descending Brilliance Qi**
- **Wei Position:** **Central Unity’s Congealed Truth Qi**
- **Shen Position:** **Profound Harmony’s Solemn Brilliance Qi**
- **You Position:** **Firm Rectitude’s Plain Harmony Qi**
- **Xu Position:** **True Origin’s Nurturing Spirit Qi**
- **Hai Position:** **Returning Yin to Face Truth Qi**

Thus the altar is complete.

**Upper-Tier Altar Diagram**
**Middle-Tier Altar Diagram**

The three altars described above are not used solely for delivering sentient beings. For all rites of petition and invocation, homage to the sages and audience with the perfected, averting calamities and atoning for transgressions, or praying for the state, one employs the **Mingmo Fu (Commanding Demons Talisman)**.

**Mingmo Incantation**
Divine radiance flashes and flickers,
Heaven is clear, darkness is bright.
Jade talismans bear Heaven’s mandate,
Sternly arrayed against demonic camps.
The sunlight of the Three Heavens,
Nine Shameful Ones lurk in concealment.
Nine Heavens’ light fills all,
Six Heavens’ yin disperses.
Mighty Heavenly Ding,
Grasp the talisman and assume form.
Hasten to summon Taokang,
Together they extend and perfect the true.
The ten thousand *qi* do not scatter,
One perfected ascends in flight.

**Nine Small Pennant Talismans**
The nine small pennants each have a head, each one foot two inches in length, made of crimson silk. At their center is the great pennant, five feet five inches long, its belly in yellow, its hands and feet with blue on the left and white on the right, to correspond to the Three *Qi*. The great pennant bears the great talisman; the small pennants bear the small talismans.

**Feiben Talisman**, recite the incantation.

**Jade of the Exorcist Lion of the Three Heavens**
**Talismanic Seal**
Lion Perfected, Exorcist Feathered Regalia.

The Office of Fiery Numen,
Nurtures and transforms beastly forms.
Five *qi* complete the body,
Ten thousand evils vanish without trace.
Repelling and expelling all foulness,
Devouring malevolent forces.
The true talisman erects the standard,
Establishing majesty and might.
Swiftly, swiftly, as the demon-quelling statutes command.

**Right: Exorcist Standard**
Carve a lion’s head from maple wood, adorned with colors as prescribed. Then take azure silk, three feet six inches in length and one foot five inches in width, and inscribe the talisman in gold paint. Affix twenty-four silver bells along its borders, strung with yellow thread and crimson cords.

**Left: Azure Dragon Feathered Regalia Talisman**
*Incantation:*
Thunder’s prosperity, nine *qi* arise,
Misty and lush, the Azure Palace.
Vital *qi* layer upon layer,
Transforming into nine dragons.
Wood Duke rides the *qi*,
His hue a verdant green.
Guard my soul,
That I may ascend to the Emperor’s palace.

**Right: White Tiger Feathered Regalia Talisman**
*Incantation:*
Western Metal’s radiant *qi*,
Fierce and mighty in execution.
Drumming roars stir the wind,
Ascending to the Great Void.
Overseeing Metal’s assembly,
Descending to the cinnabar steps.
Refining the spirit’s brilliance,
Ascending into the Jade Void.

**Front: Vermilion Phoenix Feathered Regalia Talisman**
*Incantation:*
Scorching brightness, true and mysterious,
Glowing upon the Cinnabar Heaven.
Crimson phoenix soars in flight,
Red mist thick and warm.
Yin demons and corpse impurities,
Turn to ash and smoke.
Refining spirit and *qi* to fulfillment,
Ascending to true immortality.

**Rear: Dark Warrior Feathered Regalia Talisman**
*Incantation:*
Mysterious and profound, the true *qi*,
Serene and clear as waves.
Below lies the numinous tortoise,
Devouring evil and consuming demons.
Scouring away dust and filth,
*Qi* harmoniously surging.
Nurturing my primordial essence,
Ascending to the Great Luo.

**Right: Four Numinous Beasts**
According to their directional colors, fashion banners from silk, each three feet six inches in length. Inscribe the talismans in vermilion and position them in their respective directions.

**Three Dawns Talisman**
Inscribe in vermilion lacquer with golden seal script, placing it before the Three Treasures. Prepare inkstone and write in red gold.
*Incantation:*
Cavernous yang shines resplendent,
Jade light pure and bright.
Merging with the celestial pivot,
Three *qi* mysterious and true.
Below, responding to the spirit chamber,
Essence and *qi* unite with spirit.
Descending radiance upon the altar steps,
Summoning the true and beckoning the numinous.
Demon kings bow their heads,
Ten thousand demons conceal their forms.
Heavenly perfected descend of their own,
Granting me eternal life.

**Talisman of Communion with the True**
*Incantation:*

At the borders of the Jade Capital’s realm,
Purple auroras surge and soar.
Ninefold radiance gleams resplendent,
Jade pendants and girdle-gems adorn.
True immortals cast their gaze below,
Riding jade chariots in descent.
Golden light pierces the celestial gates,
A single treasure-pearl suspended high.

**Talisman of Reaching the Numinous**
This is the talisman by which the Supreme Emperor summons the Three Realms. For altar rites and invocation, inscribe in vermilion on yellow silk, or fashion into a talismanic plaque.

*Incantation:*
The jade seal’s luminous rays
Descend from the Nine Heavens.
Perfected immortals and sages of the Cavernous Numinous,
Riding crimson steeds in procession.
Jade nectar and ambrosial dew,
Purple clouds and numinous mist.
Bowing to the Three Realms,
Before the throne of the Most High.

**Five Directions Jade Script**
When establishing an altar on borrowed ground, omit the jade characters and use only the central talismanic script.

*Incantation:*
Mysterious Emperor and exalted perfected,
Primordial Beginning and the Five Elders.
Bestowing talismans and imparting teachings,
Enabling me to practice the Dao.
This day and hour,
Transmitting the talisman and receiving the Dao,
Establishing the fast and practicing the Way.
Summoning the numinous and binding demons,
Sweeping away calamities and misfortunes.
Great deities of the Five Directions,
Reverently submit to the Three Treasures.
Following me to an auspicious end,
Attaining agelessness.
Shedding death and ascending to life,
Flourishing yet untouched by decay.
Those who defy me meet misfortune,
Living to face hardship and age.
Dying, they descend to the underworld’s paths,
To be examined in hell’s torments.

**Eastern Jade Script**

*Incantation:*
Nine qi sprout yang,
Jade calendar and dragon script.
The Eight Trigrams spread outward,
One virtue concealed within.
Transformation arises from me,
Severing death and returning to auspiciousness.

Azure Emperor attends the soul,
Nine yang cinnabar radiance.

Nine yang external origin,
Within and without, penetrating clarity.
Two, seven, four, five—
Transformation pervades the natural.

Southern peak’s three luminaries,
Qi stabilizes their brilliance.

Fire’s brightness joins virtue,

**Western Jade Script**

Great White’s flowing essence,
Seven stars guard the numinous.
Heavenly virtue inwardly preserved,
Metal and fire take no form.
That which life cannot transform,
White origin employs its clarity.

*For the Living Rite:*
Luminous white soul,
Great White’s primordial essence.
Severing and beheading demonic qi,

Great White’s essence.

Mysterious virtue and five numina,
Deliver life’s primordial One.
Embryonic essence, life’s demons,

Drifting ghostly thieves,

**Central Jade Script**
Five talismanic scripts, each direction’s color and hue,
Vermilion seal-script—
To pacify the five directions,
To suppress evil and repel wrong,

To reach the Mysterious Vault.

Lu Bangyan states: *Emerging from the Numinous Treasure, Ascending the Mysterious Canon.*

*Incantation:*
Central Lord, honored deity,
Twelve primordial perfected.
Governing the Four Great,
Primordial Jade Dawn.

*For the Living Rite:*
Yellow Center’s great deity,
Essence of the Five Phases.
Above heaven, below earth,
Penetrating the primordial root.
