Compiled by Lu Shizhong of the Song Dynasty. Thirty scrolls.
Source text: *Daoist Canon*, *Dongzhen* Section, Methods Category.

**The Supreme Mysterious Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Rites, Scroll Twenty-Two**
**Chapter Twenty-Four: Preserving and Controlling the Kalpic Turnings**

The Master said: The Great Dao gives birth to the Primordial Heaven; the Primordial Heaven gives birth to the Supreme Ultimate; the Supreme Ultimate gives birth to the Two Modes. Thereafter, the Five Phases divide, and the Eight Trigrams array themselves. Fortune and misfortune are determined, and the powers of punishment and virtue arise. Thus, Heaven holds the yang above, its three luminaries radiant and bright. Earth holds the yin below, its five peaks standing in majestic stillness. Humanity receives the numinous within, possessing all things in abundance, thereby completing the Three Powers and establishing the Ultimate.

Yet those confined by form cannot transcend their form; those bound by fate cannot escape their fate. Thus, when stars deviate from their courses, floods and fires bring great disasters. When Metal and Wood clash in punishment, the Five Phases restrain and overcome one another. Any deviation brings nothing but fortune or misfortune, leading to celestial portents: stars wander from their paths, drought and flood contend. Earthly portents: mountains collapse, waters boil, the earth quakes, seas dry up. Human portents: bandits and barbarians arise, warfare erupts in season.

Such are the calamitous fates. Therefore, the Most High established the Teachings of Great Peace, providing talismans to control them. To ensure Heaven’s enduring existence, one must first preserve and control the kalpic turnings. This chapter is established to weave through Heaven and Earth, protect the state and pacify the household, deliver people from the disasters of the *yang jiu*, and elevate the world to the fortune of Great Peace. Is this not excellent?

---

**Method for Dispelling Comets**

The Master said: Whenever comets or inauspicious stars appear, one should present the *Star-Dispelling Talisman* and recite the *Scripture of the Eleven Luminaries of the Numinous Treasure*.

**The Most High’s Star-Dispelling Talisman**
*Incantation:*
Celestial talismans traverse the world, preserving and controlling inauspicious stars.
When celestial paths lose their order, follow the talisman and align with the scripture.
The Emperor’s decree is in hand, bringing tranquility and peace.
Turning misfortune into fortune, malevolent spirits conceal their forms.
By the command of the Talisman of Great Peace, star officials obey.
As proclaimed, so shall it be.

**The Dipper’s Light for Controlling Stars**

The Master said: Use the great majestic true light of the Celestial Dipper to shatter evil and malevolence, thereby transforming calamity into blessing. Arrange the Twenty-Eight Constellations in the four directions, and within them, array the Twelve Earthly Branches, controlling them with the Dipper’s light. Place three lamps at each position, except for the central Dipper’s position and those of the Sun and Moon, where only one lamp is set. Use sesame oil, keeping the lamps alight for three days and nights, reciting the incantation at the three periods.

At each position, hang a red banner inscribed with the *Star-Dispelling Talisman*. After three days, burn them facing the Gate of Heaven.

**Incantation at the Three Periods upon the Altar**
The Dipper exists in Heaven, its might governing the starry heavens.
The power of the Dipper’s fire annihilates all misfortune.
Malevolent stars and baleful *qi* dare display their omens.
The Dipper’s fire, ten thousand *zhang* in height, purifies the ten directions.
Stars and baleful forces retreat, malevolent spirits hide in concealment.
Following the scriptures of Heaven, the nation prospers.
Receiving Heaven’s talisman, no disaster can harm.
The harmonious *qi* of the Four Heavens eternally preserve *li* and *zhen*.
Should any dare disobey, seize and deliver them to the Dipper’s might.
I invoke the teachings of the Most High Lord Lao, by command, to save and seize.
Recite secretly at the three periods, without counting repetitions.

**Ritual of Pouring Wine and Sprinkling Water**

**Method for Dispelling Solar Eclipses**

The Master said: When yin evil encroaches upon yang, the Sun and Moon are eclipsed. This method should be used to protect and dispel, ensuring all is auspicious.

**The Nine Dragons’ Yang Valley Radiance Talisman**
Make banners of red silk, inscribing this talisman eighty-one times. Plant the banners beside lamps. Nine Daoists and ritual masters, clad in crimson robes, circumambulate the lamps reciting the incantation until the light returns, then gather the talismans. Burn them facing south to dispel great disasters and bring forth auspiciousness.

*Incantation:*
The *qi* of yin demons seeks to violate the firm yang.
Nine dragons surge with light, restoring the yang’s radiance.
In an instant, clarity and brightness return, the great thousand worlds resplendent.
Yin evil and comets that encroach vanish without trace.
The crow-wheel blazes with light, all nations return to yang.
Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by statute and command.

---

**Method for Dispelling Bandits**

**Master’s Instruction on Dispelling Bandits**

The Master said: Venus, the omen of misfortune—when its course strays from its proper path, comets and baleful stars appear, also portending calamity. If bandits have not yet mobilized, they may be suppressed through ritual; if already in motion, their threat may be lightened, and they will be unable to inflict harm.

The method requires forty-nine Daoists to establish an altar, prepare the offering, and present memorials in the usual manner. At the time of the ritual, recite the *Incantation for Laying Down Arms* and bury the *Talisman for Halting Weapons* outside the western gate. Arrange the Seven Stars in their pattern, inscribing talismans on bricks and burying them likewise.

The western gate refers to the west of the capital for a kingdom, the west of the prefectural seat for a commandery, and the west of the county seat for a district. At night, light the Venus Lamp, burn the talismans, and peace will be secured.

**Method for Burying Talismans to Dispel Bandits**
Use new bricks, inscribe in cinnabar, and bury at the western gate of the city. Arrange the Seven Stars in their pattern, also inscribing talismans on bricks and burying them.

**Seven Stars Talisman for Averting Disaster**
Inscribe in cinnabar on red paper. Invoke the Star Lords governing the generals, draw *qi* to infuse the brush, and trace upon swords and halberds—wherever they are directed, none shall oppose them. Carry it on the person, and enemies will not prevail.

**Talisman for the Commander to Ward Off Poison**
Form the Dipper mudra, inscribe in purple on white paper, and hang upon a ceremonial bow and arrows for veneration.

**Talisman for Warding Off Harm**
Form the *sha* mudra, inscribe in chalk on white paper, and hang upon spears and polearms.

**Talisman for Dispelling Baleful Qi**
Inscribe in black on white paper, hang within the altar, and execute the *Flying Seven Stars Mudra*.

For these methods, keep the lamps alight for three days and nights, ascending the altar at the three ritual hours. Upon completion, present the talismans and weapon-banners to Venus, burning them at the northwestern Celestial Gate.

**Method for Dispelling Fire Disasters**

The Master said: Heaven’s punishments manifest as water and fire, but fire alone is most severe. When misfortune arises not from celestial reproach but from the calamity of Mars, this method should be employed to avert it.

**Five Qi’s Mysterious Register of Yin Radiance**
Inscribe the talisman on black silk, two feet and four inches in length, in yellow ink. Display it openly before the altar to suppress fire disasters. Inscribe it with the *Mudra of the Northern Emperor*.

*Incantation:*

The Star of Grand Yin at Chen, spirit of the Five Qi.
Subduing the flames of fire, demonic dust naturally clears.
The Supreme Emperor commands: universally protect all living beings.
Red clouds withdraw their blaze, the Fire Emperor retreats his banner.
The qi of Grand Yin, vast and boundless in the Mysterious Court.
Swiftly, swiftly, as the Law of the Dark-Life Emperor of Grand Yin commands.

Recite this incantation at the three ritual hours, thirty-six times each. Sprinkle the talisman with water until thoroughly damp.

**Talisman for Petitioning Mars to Avert Fire Disasters**
Inscribe three identical talismans on red paper with yellow ink, affix them to a vermilion banner, and plant it before the star of calamity.

*Incantation:*
By imperial decree, Mars, swiftly return your scorching banner.
Fire clouds extinguish their flames, the four borders grow solemn and clear.
The myriad people dwell in peace, baleful qi no longer taints.
By the command of this talisman, Flaming Star, heed with reverence.
Swiftly, swiftly, as the Law commands.

Use the *Noon Mudra* to conclude with *Zi*, reciting the incantation at the three ritual hours, twenty-four times each. Sprinkle the banner with water until moistened for auspiciousness.

**Diagram of Lamps to Subdue the Fire Emperor and Avert Disasters**
**Talisman to Suppress Fiery Radiance**
Fashion banners from coarse paper, each bearing twelve identical talismans, and encircle the lamp altar with them.
Alternatively, inscribe talismans on yellow paper with vermilion ink and distribute them to households for protection and aversion.
Use the *Mudra of the Northern Emperor* in all cases.

*Incantation:*

The Southern Dipper’s Fire Officials dispel poison and harm,
The Northern Dipper’s Water Spirits extinguish misfortune and calamity.
Press down with the *Kan* mudra, flick into water, or infuse into the talisman.
All requests shall be fulfilled,
All stagnation and distress shall dissolve.
Those who reverently follow the scripture’s rites with sincere devotion
Shall surely have their wishes answered, aligning with the numinous mind.
All who hold this in their hearts and constantly pay homage
Shall find no gate through which misfortune dares to enter.

Trace the steps of the Dipper, clasp the *Mudra of the Northern Emperor*,
Inscribe on yellow paper with vermilion ink,
And affix to the left and right of the central courtyard gate
To suppress fiery misfortune and welcome descending auspiciousness.

**Two Incantations to Command Fire and Extinguish Its Might**

**First Incantation:**
Northern Black Emperor, essence of *Ren* and *Gui*,
Ancestor of the Water Spirits, vast and abyssal.
Reverently summon the Dark Tortoise to subdue the Fire’s essence.
Celestial waves of numinous power vanquish *Bing* and *Ding*.
Fiery radiance is quelled, transformed into pure *yin*.
Swiftly, swiftly, as the *Taiyin Xuanming* commands.

**Second Incantation:**
*Taiyin Xuanming*, essence of primordial *qi*,
Pure *yin* coalesces to subdue the brilliance of *Li*.
Black waves surge and billow, red light scatters into *yin*.
Within lies the Divine Lord, clad in black, dwelling in the Water Court.
Able to subdue the Fire’s malevolence, the Primordial Sovereign.
Mighty springs churn waves, *Jia Shen* and *Cheng Ming* resplendent.
Roaring and bellowing, dragons cry *ji sha hong*.
Waves surge in all four directions, *yin* *qi* congeals in chaos.
The Fire of *Li* retreats, its radiance vanishes.
By the command of the Most High, the Fire Spirit obeys.
Swiftly, swiftly, as the *Taiyin Xuanming* commands.

After reciting the incantations over the lamps and banners, sprinkle with water,
And the Fire Star shall return to its place, the Fire Spirit retreat,
Turning misfortune into fortune.

**Method to Avert Earthquakes**
The Master says: Heaven moves while Earth is still,
For the heavens revolve above while the earth rests below—
This is the constant principle of *yin* and *yang*.
If the earth, receiving celestial influence, trembles and quakes,
It is because *yin* and *yang* have fallen out of order.
This method should be employed to avert it.

The practitioner shall first establish an altar,
Set up a sacrifice to the Earth Deity *Houtu*,
Then petition the *Kun* direction, and consecrate the *Purple-Written Jade Register*.
Prepare the *Jade Characters to Pacify Kun*,
Then disperse the altar.

**Purple-Written Jade Register to Pacify Kun**
Use cypress wood, two *chi* and four *cun* in length, six *cun* in width,
Inscribe the talisman in yellow, with the *Yu Qing* mudra.
Face the *Kun* direction of the city,
Bury it three *chi* and six *cun* deep in the earth.

**Incantation:**
The Five Peaks stabilize *Kun*,
The Nine Sovereigns uphold Earth’s order.
Gold and jade nurture flourishing refinement,
Mountains and rivers channel numinous *qi*.
The four corners stand firm without tilting,
The Nine Tripods naturally hold their place.
The August Spirits ensure eternal peace,
*Houtu* governs with equanimity.
Swiftly, swiftly, as the *Zhonghuang Anzhen* commands.

Recite nine times at each of the three ritual hours.
Burn the *Talisman to Pacify Kun’s Directions*.

**Jade Talisman to Pacify Kun’s Directions**
Inscribe on yellow paper with vermilion ink,
Burn at the *Kun* direction, using the incantation as the petition.

**Incantation:**
*Kun*’s directions are pacified and still,
The Nine Lands are at peace.
The earthen ramparts bear the talisman,
For ten thousand years without tilting.
Malevolence and omens disperse,
Joy and great peace prevail.
As the command decrees. **Great Talisman of Pacification**

On yellow paper inscribed with vermilion ink, place before *Houtu* and perform the rites with incense at the three ritual hours.

**Method to Dispel Locusts**
The Master says: Heaven’s calamities manifest as floods, droughts, locusts, and pests—all harming crops and bringing famine. The karmic force of sentient beings invokes these afflictions; Heaven has no intent. The Most High, in boundless compassion, provides this exorcism so the people may dwell in peace.

Locusts arise when winter snow fails to fall, and insects breed within the yin. The malevolent, borne by fire, grow wings and take flight in summer, ravaging seedlings and crops. The eggs of these pests, once touched by the *qi* of snow, burrow three *chi* into the earth. After three snows, they descend nine *chi*. If snow is absent for a year, they rise three *chi*; if scarce for three years, drought follows, and locusts emerge as a plague.

To suppress and dispel them, erect an altar and hold a *jiao* ritual. Dispatch officials to drive them into water with drums and wind, and petition the *Fú* Spirit to gather the malevolent insects.

**Talisman to Dispel Locusts**
Inscribe on yellow paper with vermilion ink. Face the *Xun* direction, pace the Dipper, and burn the talisman. Turn toward the south, recite the incantation thirty-six times, and spray water. After three days, if the ritual succeeds, wind will rise and locusts will enter the water.

Also, take two chestnut boards, inscribe a talisman on each, and nail one where the locusts originated. Erect the other on a high frame and burn it with chestnut wood.

**Incantation:**
Flames of the Vermilion Bird of the south,
Blazing with the might of *Bing* and *Ding*.
Wings born of lost salvation,
Spawned like dust in swarms.
The Nine August Ones conceal primordial chaos,
Auspicious snow drives them into hiding.
Fire’s *qi* breeds malevolence,
Nurturing harm to the roots of crops.
I summon the Earth God and the Lord of Locusts,
The *Fú* Spirit of command.
Drums stir boundless winds,
Sweeping them into the sea’s depths.
Malevolent pests scatter,
Crops rejoice in autumn’s harvest.
Swiftly, swiftly, as the law commands.

**Method to Pray for Rain During Drought**
The Master says: When prolonged drought persists despite prayers, local officials must act with compassion for the people. Submit a petition at the altar, beseeching rain. The ritual master prepares the words, submitting memorials to the Three Heavens and the Heavenly Master’s court, and petitions all relevant realms.

Then, open the altar, pace the *gang*, perform the rites, and summon the dragon spirits, with three, five, or seven days as the standard. Once rain falls sufficiently, hold a separate *jiao* to give thanks. If the rain is inadequate, use the method to hasten it.

**Talisman to Summon Dragons**
Inscribe on black paper with vermilion ink. Pace the Dipper beneath the moon, face the *gang* to gather *qi*, and affix the talisman to the petition. Dispatch the Heavenly Soldiers to summon the dragon spirits, who will arrive at once.

**Talisman to Drive Dragons and Bring Rain**
Inscribe on black paper with white powder. Burn in the incense censer, offering incense thrice daily—great efficacy is assured.

**Incantation:**
Heaven and earth’s *qi* unite,
Yin and yang harmonize.
Dragons ride clouds and mist—
Dare they disobey?
Sweet rains moisten the land,
Drought demons vanish.
Swiftly, swiftly, as the law commands.

After reciting, face the moon, turn toward the *gang*, and spray water. If no response comes in three days, cast the iron talisman.

**The Most High’s Talisman to Drive Rain**
Inscribe with vermilion on an iron plaque. Pace the *gang*, wield the sword, and dispatch the Heavenly Soldiers to gather *qi* from the celestial *gang* before casting it into rivers or lakes.

**Upper Clarity Talisman to Invoke Rain**
An iron tablet, two *cun* and four *fen* wide, two *chi* and four *cun* long, inscribed with vermilion. Seal in a double-layered pouch and cast into a dragon’s cave. Retrieve it once the rain is sufficient.

All talismans follow the above methods. When casting iron talismans, choose deep, numinous pools within the domain—shallow waters are ineffective. If no springs or caves are present, use a numinous well. Near rivers or lakes, cast into them for greater efficacy.

When casting the talisman, do not look back, lest sudden thunderstorms arise. Such is the swiftness of this response—proceed with care.

*The Supreme Mysterious Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method, Scroll Twenty-Two Concludes*

*The Supreme Mysterious Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method*
**Scripture Title:** *The Supreme Mysterious Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method*
Compiled by Lu Shizhong of the Song Dynasty. Thirty scrolls in total.
**Source Text:** *Daoist Canon of the Zhengtong Era*, *Dongzhen* Section, Methods Category.

---

*The Supreme Mysterious Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method, Scroll Twenty-Three*
**Chapter Twenty-Five: Severing Corpse Parasites**

The Master said: Those born in the Lower Era are ever beset by calamities. In this degenerate age, the roots of death pass unbroken from one generation to the next. Of all afflictions, corpse parasites are the most pernicious—transmitted by the Nine Worms, yet also arising when ordinary men exhaust their minds, deplete their strength, injure their *qi*, and squander their essence. Once the true [essence] is depleted at its root, perverse [influences] begin to spread without limit. Thus, the Mysterious Origin pities the world and provides methods for healing.

Yet the manifestations of illness are manifold, and the modes of contagion vary. Even houses and food may gradually transmit [the affliction], while clothing and *qi* readily entangle [the victim]. Only by severing the roots of death can one hope to restore the *qi* of life. Therefore, this chapter presents methods to relieve suffering and toil.

---

**Method for Treating House-Transmitted [Disease]**
The Master said: In abandoned dwellings and empty rooms, where human traces seldom reach, the *qi* of illness lingers even after years have passed. When a house stands vacant, its chambers sealed and stagnant, yin darkness congeals, and perverse *qi* fails to disperse—thus, the poison of suffering remains. Whoever first opens the door and enters receives its toxin; those with weakened spirits suffer its misfortune.

At the onset of infection, the hair bristles, the spine and back grow cold with shivers—these are its signs. The disease lurks in the numinous palace, lodges in the Mud Pill, and spreads to the four limbs. Over time, the illness finally erupts: gasping, coughing blood, flesh and bones withering, alternating chills and fever, dreams and spirits inverted—these are the symptoms of house-transmitted [disease].

To sever house-transmitted [disease], one must reside where contagion has occurred. After one month, swiftly return to the Great Dao and administer urgent treatment—then eight or nine out of ten will recover. Otherwise, as the contagion deepens over time, the disease grows more severe, and death draws near. Even divine power will be of no avail.

**Talisman for Treating House-Transmitted [Disease]**
Take a new brick, grind raw cinnabar in sunlight, face east, clasp the Northern Emperor mudra, and gather solar *qi* to inscribe it. On a *jia* or *ding* day at noon, bury it in the central courtyard at a depth of three *chi* and six *cun*. At the moment of burial, the ritual master paces the *gang*, wields the sword, sprays water, transforms into the Celestial Snail, and recites the incantation:

**Incantation:**
*"Hark! Ghostly convulsions, swiftly depart the central courtyard!
The *gang* fire towers ten thousand *zhang*, lightning flashes and bells stream.
Scatter the ghostly *qi* with burning, sever and strike down demonic spirits.
Corpse-transmitting and pestilence ghosts—hear this talisman and flee at once!
Plunge ten thousand *zhang* into the earth, dissolve into fine dust.
Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by law!"*

**Talismans for the Four Corners and Eight Directions of the Patient’s Room**
Inscribe on catalpa or cypress slips with cinnabar, then nail them to the eight directions. Use the *qi* of the Three Origins’ Demon-Slaying Talisman to purge perverse *qi*, after which tranquility will prevail.

**Method for Inscribing the Talismans:**
Transform the spirit, pace the *gang*, revolve the body into the Dipper, and draw *qi* to inscribe them.

**East**
**West**

**South**
**North**
**Northeast**
**Southeast**
**Southwest**
**Northwest**

**Incantation for Nailing the Talismans:**
The heavens hold true *qi*, the Dipper’s majesty shines.
Shatter demons, subdue spirits, expel all misfortune.
Heavenly soldiers stand in ranks, lightning flashes fly.
Golden spears and iron steeds spread across the vault of heaven.
Seize and capture pestilent spirits, sever *zhu* and dispel calamity.
You are a flying *jing* ghost, a corpse-transmitting plague.
Hear my divine incantation—flee at once to other lands.
Behold my sacred talisman—scatter to the four directions.
Begone, begone! If you do not leave, you will be seized and bound to the *kuigang*.
Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by law!

**Method for Treating Clothing Transmission**
The master says: Clothing transmission occurs when the living share bedding with the afflicted or contract illness through garments. Once the patient dies, their clothes, curtains, outerwear, and utensils must be steamed, for foul *qi* and pestilential infestations lurk within. Miserly households may reuse them, while the poor cannot replace them, thus nurturing disaster—how tragic!

When the disease first takes hold, nights are restless, the spirit is unsettled, essence is lost in dreams, and night sweats alternate with chills and fever. If perverse *qi* lodges in the skin and hair and is left untreated for a month, it penetrates the bones; after two months, it enters the organs. When perverse *qi* gathers in the spirit’s abode and remains untreated for a month, it spreads to the limbs; after two months, it invades the marrow. When perverse *qi* entangles the soul and spirit for three months, the illness solidifies into malevolent *qi*. If it enters the organs and is left untreated for a month, the disease manifests. From this, we see that prompt treatment is paramount. Though this great method exists, if not applied early, its efficacy may falter.

---

**Methods for Treating Clothing Transmission**

For the method of treating clothing transmission, use talismans to fumigate the garments, then roll them up with the talisman and cast them into flowing water—do not look back. If the illness has not yet taken form, ingest the *Three Luminaries Qi Talisman* for a month, and recovery may follow. If the disease has persisted for two or three months, it may be difficult to cure. After one month, the *Inquiry and Relief Talisman* must be employed.

**Talisman for Treating Clothing Transmission**
Assume the Dipper Hand Seal, face the moon’s establishment, and recite the names of the Dipper thirty-six times. Dip the brush and inscribe the talisman, then fumigate with its smoke to attain peace. Next, place the talisman with the object and cast it into flowing water—do not turn back to look. The incantation reads:

*"The celestial talisman bears command, entering the Dipper’s midst.
Ghosts and spirits tremble in fear, vanquishing malevolent forces.
The Azure Dragon guards the left, the White Tiger the right.
The Vermilion Bird leads ahead, the Dark Warrior follows behind.
Transmitted afflictions and flying corpses—traces and tracks obliterated.
Should any dare remain, the Dipper’s fire and flying blades shall strike.
Buried ten thousand fathoms deep, their bodies melted in flame.
Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by law!"*

**Method for Treating Food Transmission**
The Master says: The method for treating food transmission arises when one inadvertently consumes the remnants of a patient’s food, drink, or medicine, thereby contracting their pathogenic *qi* in the heart and abdomen, which may also cause illness. Generally, food transmission is still treatable, but transmission through dwellings or clothing allows perverse *qi* to penetrate deeply, making the affliction severe and difficult to remedy. In food transmission, if the patient has not yet died, the pathogenic *qi* has not fully taken hold, so it remains treatable. If treatment is delayed, however, it may become incurable over time, evolving into a grave illness—this must not be overlooked.

The method employs thirty-six talismans, burned together to produce smoke, which the patient must inhale and swallow—force them if necessary—until both talismans and smoke are fully consumed. Initially, fumigation may be difficult, but after some time, it becomes easier. The patient may feel phlegm rising in the throat and should cough and spit it out. Copious sputum and coughing, especially thick saliva, are particularly favorable. If the pathogenic *qi* is shallow, phlegm will be scant; if deep, violent vomiting with profuse saliva will occur, ensuring recovery. Once the perverse *qi* is expelled, further fumigation is unnecessary. Instead, ingest the *Three Luminaries Talisman* to replenish depleted *qi* and restore vitality. For a month, strictly avoid alcohol, lust, joy, and anger to ensure peace.

**Talisman for Treating Food Transmission**
Assume the Dipper Hand Seal, align with the Dipper’s *qi*, and inscribe thirty-six talismans on yellow paper with cinnabar. Burn them as incense. The incantation reads:

*"Solemnly command the soul’s essence, luminous and radiant.
The Three Fields grow tranquil, the corpse’s spirit flees its form.
Laboring ghosts disperse, the Nine *Qi* unite as one.
The talisman’s Dipper swiftly slays, no laboring affliction shall intrude.
Flying infestations hasten away, ghostly maladies turn to dust.
Piercing limbs and entering the abdomen, all malevolent vapors swept clean.
True *qi* guards the body, upright *qi* endures forever.
Swiftly, swiftly, as decreed by law!"*

**General Method for Treating Corpse Transmission**
The Master says: In treating corpse transmission, one must understand its intricacies. Among the Nine Worms, six transmit across six generations, while three do not. The stomach worm, roundworm, and tapeworm may arise from visceral toxins or familial transmission, passing down the six worms. Roughly every ten days, they traverse the four limbs in cycles, repeating endlessly. They feed every three days, retreating after five, and during their active phase, the body aches as they consume flesh. When they retreat, they return to their lairs, inducing a drunken stupor lasting five days, during which the illness temporarily subsides. This is the opportune moment to administer talismans and medicine. Otherwise, the worms grow accustomed to the power of talismans and remedies, making treatment difficult.

A single worm occupies twelve lairs in the body; six worms occupy seventy-two. In a month, the first ten days see them travel from the heart to the head, roaming four lairs. The middle ten days, from the heart to the navel, roaming four limbs. The last ten days, from the navel to the feet, roaming four limbs. When administering medicine or talismans, this cycle must be observed. Thus, the classic states: Treatment within sixty days yields an eighty to ninety percent success rate. Within one hundred eighty days, thirty to forty percent. Beyond this, survival is uncertain.

Those who pursue the worms’ original essence among the people often employ deceptive techniques, fabricating worms for profit—conduct befitting beasts. Instead, ingest the *Purple Court Talisman* at night, prepare an oil cauldron, and keep the surroundings brightly lit. The moment live worms appear, capture and fry them in oil, then cast them into flowing water—do not look back. However, success occurs in only one or two out of ten cases, for such forces cannot be defied. If the patient’s illness is mild, the worms may be invisible and untraceable, appearing only in dreams as figures bidding farewell—this is the sign. The *Purple Court Talisman* for pursuing worms is recorded in the *Celestial Heart Method: Talismans and Scripts* of this teaching. The procedures for pursuing worms are detailed in the *Celestial Heart* of our ancestral tradition. Later inheritors of this teaching must practice with reverence, for its efficacy is as evident as a shadow following form. Do not disclose it lightly. Guard it well.

**Conclusion of *The Supreme Mysterious Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method*, Scroll Twenty-Three**

**Title:** *The Supreme Mysterious Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method*
**Compiler:** Lu Shizhong of the Song Dynasty
**Volumes:** Thirty
**Source:** *Daoist Canon*, *Dongzhen* Section, Methods Category

**Principles of *The Supreme Mysterious Origin Three Heavens Jade Hall Great Method*, Scroll Twenty-Four**
**Chapter Twenty-Six: Prolonging Life and Averting Misfortune**

The Master says: Those bound by fate cannot escape it; those confined by form cannot transcend it. Thus, the *Lingbao Scripture* states: Even the sun, moon, and five planets wax and wane. The most sagely and divine beings experience rise and decline. How much more so for the unlearned, who suffer illness and injury.

These all are those bound by fate and confined by form. Thus arises the method for averting misfortune and prolonging life. Yet if one’s form transcends the formless, if one’s fate merges with the fathomless, if things bear no blemish, if spirits emit no ominous resonance—what misfortune could there be to avert?

Nevertheless, worldly people remain ensnared in the dusty net, stained by illusory attachments and habitual defilements. Without the salvific power of ritual dissolution, how could they escape the torment of calamity and peril? Moreover, hunger and satiety, toil and exertion, heat and dampness, wind and cold—any deviation from proper regulation may readily harm the primordial *qi*. Further, when stars of annual misfortune descend in conjunction, when monthly afflictions align upon the body, when yearly and cyclical forces clash, when dwellings prove inauspicious, when vows made to heaven are spoken with duplicity, when curses cast upon others rebound upon oneself, when malevolent spirits possess women, when flying earth and flying calamity startle and injure infants—even the slightest lapse may trigger disaster. Without recourse to the subtle and profound, who could transcend such trials?

Therefore, this chapter expounds in detail the methods for delivering others.

**The Secret Memorial to the Dipper for Averting Misfortune**
Alas! The unlearned, deluded by the dust of toil; the urban and courtly, buried in the pursuit of profit and rank—desiring to cherish life yet lacking means to prolong it, wishing to escape misfortune yet devoid of methods to avert it. All this stems from fate’s predetermination and the constraints of form. Since their embodiment has not yet penetrated the true and real, they naturally struggle to withstand the turning of karmic cycles. Whenever the hundred-and-six calamities threaten, secretly memorializing the Dipper of the lofty heavens becomes the secret to preserving life and ensuring wholeness, the mystery of dispelling disaster and atoning for transgressions. This method serves as the urgent recourse for ordinary people, the vital path to reviving life. Yet if one cultivates the supreme Dao, awakens to true emptiness, possesses abundant *qi* and complete spirit, enjoys bodily peace and well-being—why would one need to borrow another’s power for ritual dissolution?

**Purification Altar Talisman**
For purifying all altars and dissolving impurities, use this talisman. First, transform the spirit into the attire of a perfected one, visualize nine phoenixes crowning the head, the four numinous beasts arrayed in guard, radiance manifesting before the fingers, and the four Dippers shielding the body.

*Incantation:* □□□□□□□.
Visualize the Dipper entering the water.

Summon with reverence the Seven Stars of the Northern Dipper, the essence of the stars, to descend into the water. All ghosts of myriad afflictions, swiftly depart ten thousand leagues—those who do not shall be slain. Western Venus Youth, hasten! As the statute commands.

*Great Purification Incantation:*
Oṃ vāli oṃ vāli huṃ nauli tuṣṭa kroḍa kṣa kha svāhā.

The Seven Talismans for Prolonging Life are found in the *Chapter on Prolonging Life and Delivering from Calamity*.

**Jade Clarity Mudra for Paper-Twist Talismans**
At the moment of first lighting the lamp, take one lamp talisman and fashion it into a paper twist to light the lamp. In spring and summer, begin from *Kui*; in autumn and winter, begin from *Pou*.

Next, take one talisman and burn it in the incense burner, reciting the incantation:
Spirits summoned, spirits arrive; sages summoned, sages attend. Transform this divine talisman, unite with the luminous heart of Heaven. Hasten! As the statute commands.

Supreme Highest Clarity, safeguard life and prolong existence. The Six Harmonies and Three Officials, the myriad jade spirits of the Dao. Heaven dissolves, earth is at peace, the Seven Stars assemble in solemnity. Purple clouds bear the load, soaring to ascend to Highest Clarity.

When awaiting the brightening of the Seven Stars, recite the incantation:
Heaven is profound, earth is shallow, the sun and moon revolve. The Five Stars perpetually move, stirring my celestial image. I establish one altar—ten thousand ghosts all submit. With one stroke of the divine blade, ten thousand ghosts scatter. Hasten! As the statute commands.

Next, present the memorial.

Arrange the ritual positions, and supplicate the Northern Dipper’s Mysterious Numinous Seven Primordial Life-Protecting Star Lords: Here stands so-and-so, who approaches the Great Dao, beseeching repentance and protection. Your servant now follows ancient rites, solemnly establishing the Seven Star Lamps, erecting the altar for a secret offering, and proceeding as prescribed—arraying and kindling the pure lamps to divine fortune and misfortune.

Your servant now calms the spirit and steadies the will, nurturing qi and returning to the spirit. At this auspicious moment, I submit this memorial, humbly entreating the Imperial Perfected Ones to descend and condescend to witness my sincere heart, granting your servant’s petition. The remaining details shall be proclaimed in the secret offering ritual.

Next, in utmost reverence, I invite the Seven Primordials to descend, receive this memorial, and through the brightness or dimness of the lamps, discern fortune or misfortune. By the power of your majestic numen, may all wishes be fulfilled.

Next, circumambulate the lamps three times, reciting the incantation forty-nine times:
Bright lamps gather light, wandering spirits do not flee.
The seven po return to their abodes, the myriad spirits all submit.
At midday, shadows align, ever dwelling in radiance.
Hasten! As the statute commands.

Recite further:
Following the celestial stem, erecting the Dipper, the ritual torch ignites the stars.
The Seven Kings descend—primordial, prosperous, steadfast, and upright.

Next, establish the central lamp facing the Dipper, burn the talismans in sequence into each lamp’s basin, and visualize the circulation as prescribed. Place the life talisman in a water basin before the lamps.

Divining by the Lamps:
At the *Greedy Wolf* lamp, divine one’s position—brightness portends fortune, dimness misfortune.
At the *Giant Gate* lamp, divine lifespan—brightness is auspicious, dimness ominous.
At the *Salary Storage* lamp, divine fortune and virtue—brightness is fortunate; dimness calls for expiation, almsgiving, and prayer.
At the *Literary Brilliance* lamp, divine official rank—brightness brings promotion, dimness stagnation.
At the *Integrity Chastity* lamp, divine marriage—brightness signifies union, dimness separation.
At the *Military Brilliance* lamp, divine illness—brightness brings recovery, dimness suffering.
At the *Broken Army* lamp, divine servants, disputes, conflicts, or pursuit of thieves—brightness brings success, dimness failure.

For households divining illness or misfortune, observe the seven lamps of the Dipper. One must be devout, wholeheartedly attending to the signs and offering repayment. Sweep and purify the ritual chamber, ensuring no gaps; do not permit women to peer in, and guard against cats or dogs disrupting the space. Burn fine incense in a blazing fire, and perform the rite in the stillness of night.

If the lamps burn brightly with long, steady flames, all affairs shall be auspicious. If the lamps are dim with short, scattered, or flickering flames, misfortune looms.

A blue flame signals a lingering corpse in the dwelling—qi stagnation invites exorcism, quarrels, restless nights, and disturbances among the young and yin.
A red flame signals wandering souls, plague ghosts, earthly calamities, blood taboos, flying soil, or sudden disasters and anomalies.
A white flame signals legal disputes, external mourning, fright, terror, or household unrest.
A black flame signals theft, loss, inauspicious travel, lingering illness, earthly offenses, or unfulfilled vows.
If the flame dims then brightens, or brightens then dims, ancestors seek offerings, and kin bring misfortune.
If the initial light is unsteady or the oil spills, spirits and ghosts swarm, demons press urgently, laboring insects fly or hide, the sick do not recover, and birth ghosts intrude—such signs defy reversal by prayer.

For any of the above anomalies, redouble devotion, pray earnestly, and perform the Dipper-pacing rite to subdue them. Do not be negligent.

Life Talisman:
Invite the descent into the offering.

Next, examine the lamps and present the memorial, subduing and controlling as prescribed.

The master says: In presenting the memorial, use truthful words, not ornate language, lest one incur the sin of frivolous speech. Beware.

First, compose the spirit and steady the will, performing nine bows. Next, dispatch the officials as prescribed. Then pace the Nine Numinosities, contemplating the nine qi. Kneel lengthily, silently submit the memorial, then perform eight bows while presenting it. Visualize your body as a circular azure light, with the Niwan Palace housing a Dipper-shaped star lord, ascending in sequence to the Celestial Gate.

Next, visualize the Northern Dipper’s nine palaces in the heavens, each radiant:
1. Jade Tower of Azure City.
2. Five-Colored Jade Tower.
3. Yellow Terrace Jade Tower.
4. Vermilion Terrace Jade Tower.
5. White Terrace Jade Tower.
6. Mysterious Terrace Jade Tower.
7. Nine-Colored Primal Qi Jade Tower.
8. Purple Qi Jade Tower.
9. Purple Mansion Jade Tower.

Each emits golden light, intersecting with the golden light of the nine palaces within your body. Next, press your tongue against the upper palate, transforming it into a golden bridge connecting the Yellow Path across the void to the Dipper’s mouth. Circulate the plain yellow qi of the Nine Palaces, filling them above and linking to the golden bridge below.

Next, dispatch the Three and Five Merit Officials and the Hidden Numinous Scribes to ascend the bridge. Behold embroidered-robed messengers and the two *Dhuta* envoys bearing the memorial, prostrating beneath the bridge to await commands. After a long while, a golden light ten thousand zhang long descends from the Nine Emperors of the nine palaces, entering the Niwan through the crown. Behold the nine stars of the Niwan merging into one.

Next, bow at the altar’s base and secretly recite the incantation:
I possess the Three Primordials and Three Imperial Ministers,
Their flowing light and blessings guard my form.
Above the Niwan, the Heavenly Imperial Minister,
Engraves the character *Zhao* in the Central Mystery, giving birth.
In the Crimson Palace, the Left Assistant Minister,
Firms the character *Guang* in the Four Transformations’ numen.
Below the Yellow Court, the Right Assistant Minister,
Returns to the character *Ming* in the Valley’s Mystery.
Entering the Emperor’s chamber, ascending to Highest Clarity,
I soar on clouds, phoenixes and simurghs cry.
Hasten! As the statute commands.

Next, recite further invocations, then the *Nahan Official Numen Incantation*, followed by the *Twenty-Four Perils Crossing*, and finally the *Central Heaven Great Spirit Incantation* to the *Primordial Emperor’s Upright Qi*. Gather the nine-colored lights into a sphere, perfectly bright, so that your form is unseen—only the seven stars’ light within the circulating nine qi.

After a long while, withdraw, open your eyes, and perform the offering as prescribed.

**Nahan Official Numen Incantation**
Heavenly numen, flourishing in glory,
May it safeguard long life.
Of the Great Mystery’s One,
Guard its true form.
The Five Viscera Spirit Lords,
Each preserve peace and tranquility.
Hasten! As the statute commands.

**Star-Canopy Rite**
The Master says: When a household suffers unrest, enduring years of calamity and illness, entangled in official disputes, lawsuits, or strife, with deaths following one after another, or fires and thefts recurring unceasingly—first examine whether the person has cultivated goodness and accumulated virtue, free from grave transgressions. Only then may the petition be accepted and the Star-Canopy bestowed. This rite is of utmost gravity and must not be undertaken lightly.

First, submit a memorial to the Emperor-Teacher, and petition the Seven Stars Palace of the Northern Dipper, the Eastern Florescence Prefecture, and the Southern Prosperity Bureau, beseeching that the person’s name be entrusted beneath the Northern Dipper. For example:
- Those born in the *zi* (Rat) hour: entrust their name to the Northern Dipper’s *Noble Wolf Star*, the Heavenly Gate King’s Palace.
- Those born in the *chou* (Ox) or *hai* (Pig) hours: entrust their name to the Northern Dipper’s *Great Gate Star Lord*, the Lesser Minister King’s Palace.
The rest follow accordingly.

The duration is set for one year. The rite is performed at the direction of the Canopy of Flowers, aligning with the first, second, third, and fourth months to the positions of *zi* (north), *wu* (south), *mao* (east), and *you* (west), cycling in perpetuity. Take a pillar, two *cun* and four *fen* in circumference—crafted from gold, bronze, silver, or iron according to means—one *chi* and two *cun* in length, symbolizing the twelve months of a year. Engrave seven segments upon it, each with one aperture, representing the Seven Kingly Palaces. Bury it in a pure vessel, one *chi* and two *cun* deep in the *kan* (Water) earth. On a yellow silk cloth, one *chi* and two *cun* in size, inscribe the talismanic characters of the Threefold Northern Dipper’s imperial decree and the Heavenly Stem Spirit Seal, then place it within the vessel. Additionally, file a document with the City God. Its summary states:

The Great Ming State, in such-and-such a prefecture, ward, village, and household of so-and-so, petitions on behalf of certain individuals for such-and-such a matter, pledging their lives and destinies to the Seven Kingly Palaces of the Northern Dipper. They humbly request the dispatch of officials and clerks, along with the household’s Controller of Fate and Earth God, to guard and protect them. Upon the completion of the one-year term, the vessel shall be opened, and a grand jiao offering shall be held to express gratitude.

Each person shall, according to their age, thread a strip of silk through the aperture, and all shall be placed within the vessel. Additionally, take an iron lid, bore a hole in its base to match the precious pillar, and inscribe three talismans within. When lowering the vessel, stand the precious pillar inside it, then fit the lid over the vessel’s mouth, aligning it with the apertures of the Seven Kingly Palaces. Further, use an iron plate, two *cun* wide and seven *cun* long, inscribe upon it the Threefold Northern Dipper’s imperial decree and the Heavenly Stem Spirit Seal, and affix it to the reverse side of the aperture, securing it to the lid’s base with crimson silk.

Next, prepare a new gold-lacquered bucket, two *chi* and four *cun* in height and width, to enclose the vessel, precious pillar, and iron talisman. Fill the surrounding space with pure earth, seal it tightly, and cover it with a large table, draping it with a tablecloth. Arrange the divine seats of the supervising deities upon it, and offer incense morning and evening. If no existing structure stands at the *huagai* direction, construct a small shelter to cover it.

When lowering the vessel, first arrange the sacred seats. On the preceding night, light the Lamp of Extended Life inscribed with the imperial decree. The next morning, proceed to the designated direction, burn incense, perform the divine step of the Dipper, and clasp the Dipper mudra while facing *kan* (Water). Recite the incantation:

Heaven is my canopy,
Earth is my support.
The Northern Dipper’s suspended stars
Are my raiment.
I conceal my name within the Seven Kingly Palaces,
At the heart of flowing fire,
To attain long life, transcend fate,
And enjoy a hundredfold well-being.
The *zhi* cannot harm me,
The *gan* cannot harm me.
Those who aid me are the Great Yang;
Those who oppose me shall perish.
Swiftly, swiftly, as the Emperor decrees.

Then visualize the *qi* of the *gang* filling the *kan* earth, envision the precious pillar as a palace of jade and crystal, and cast the money and silk into the vessel. As the pillar is lowered, affix the talisman, seal the lid, burn incense again, clasp the Dipper mudra, and recite the Great Divine Incantation of the Northern Dipper’s Celestial Center. Command the guardian spirits to their posts, then present offerings of wine, fruit, paper money, and spirit horses to the vessel’s guardians.

After one year, when opening the vessel, perform the same visualization and transformation as before. At the vessel’s location, recite the Opening Incantation:

Northern Dipper’s seven stars,
Pivot of the Supreme Emperor.
Preserve life, protect destiny,
Augment fortune and blessings.
As the stellar cycle completes,
All calamities dissolve.
Open this vessel,
To report above to the Pure Capital.
Guardian spirits,
Return each to your abode.
Swiftly, swiftly, as the Emperor decrees.

Then dismantle the vessel, retrieve the talismans and silk from within, and burn them during the jiao offering. Additionally, submit a petition in advance to the relevant authorities to recall the soldiers and generals, and issue documents to dismiss and return the guardian troops.

**Required Documents:**
Petition of the Stellar Patron.

**Petition of the Perfected Master.**
**Memorial to the Seven Palaces of the Kings.**
**Memorial to the Eastern Peak.**
**Document to the Officers and Generals of the Altar.**
**Document to the City God.**
**Writs to the Earth Gods and other deities.**

**Sacred Positions of the Vessel’s Lid:**
The Eleven Luminaries of Supreme Purity.
The Three Terraces and Canopy Star Lords.
The Six Controllers of the Southern Dipper.
The Seven Kings of the Northern Dipper, the Nine August Ones, and the Star Officials of the Original Destiny.
The Lord of the Eastern Peak.
The Officers of the Year-Star and the Cyclical Signs.

All the above are arrayed in their proper positions. The guardian officers and generals are arrayed to the sides. Incense is burned morning and evening daily. On the Three Primes, the Eight Festivals, and the birthdays of the destiny-stars, offerings are made to each position according to one’s means.

**Pillar Inscription (Text Beneath the Talisman):**
On the day of such-and-such a month in the year of the Year-Star, the disciples of such-and-such a prefecture, county, village, and so forth, entrust their bodies and lives to the Seven Palaces of the Northern Dipper. We humbly invoke the Great Yang, the Great Yin, the Five Planets, the Four Luminaries, the Three Terraces, the Canopy, the Southern Asterism, the Northern Dipper, the Star Lords of Original Destiny, the Three Officials, the Four Sages, the Eight Great Vajras, the Nine Heavenly Perfected Ladies, the Dharma-Protecting Kings of the Ten Directions, the Six Dings and Six Jias, the Heavenly Soldiers, the Mighty Warriors, the Envoys of the Five Thunders, the Earl of Wind, the Master of Rain, the Twenty-Four Qi, the Seventy-Two Seasonal Nodes, the Year-Star, the Great Yin, the Cyclical Signs, the various officers, the City God, the Earth Rulers, the Household Deities, the Controller of Destiny, and all the inner and outer spirits to descend. May the true qi of the Radiant Light descend into the vessel, so that the disciples, so-and-so and others, may have their calamities dissolved and their blessings and felicity amassed.

All as decreed by the August Emperor.

The dharma-positions are duly recorded, names inscribed, and seals affixed according to ritual protocol.

**Method for Dispelling Pestilence**

The Master said: People live in the world, recklessly exhausting body and mind, deluded by the physical form, unable to circulate and nurture their qi. Thus, wind, cold, summerheat, and dampness assail them from without, while excesses of desire, wine, and food ravage them from within. This causes the true qi of the Four Great Elements in the body to decline, leaving one weak in strength and weary in spirit. When the essence and marrow falter, the primordial qi becomes unstable, and pestilential diseases arise.

If one could regulate daily life to avoid cold and heat, moderate diet, nurture the illusory body, sever excessive desires to stabilize the primordial essence, and cultivate the true heart to follow the Supreme Dao, then body and spirit would both attain perfection. Qi and blood would radiate brilliance, and one would ascend to transcendence—how then could one suffer from malignant diseases or seek methods to subdue them?

The *Medical Classic* states: *"Store essence in winter, and one will not fall ill with pestilence in spring."* This is no empty saying.

Now, out of the Most High’s compassion, a method of subjugation is established to deliver those who have lost their true nature and fallen into the kalpas. May they avoid encountering demonic afflictions, and may all people attain benevolence and longevity—this is the fundamental intent of the Most High’s love for life.

Formerly, I once asked the Master: *"From what cause does this illness arise?"*
The Master replied: *"If one is harmed by cold in winter, pestilence arises in spring. If one is injured by wind in spring, diarrhea occurs in summer. If one is affected by summerheat in summer, malaria and dysentery follow in autumn. If one is struck by dampness in autumn, coughing ensues in winter. This is the general pattern. All are due to the unbalanced qi of the four seasons invading the numinous spirit, where the perverse assails the upright, giving rise to calamity and peril. Thus, the Five Phases are the root of harm to the body, each overcoming and destroying the other. Pestilence arises from the mutual conquest of the Five Phases, hence it is called the Five Pestilences."*

The Master said: *"The discourse on gods and ghosts began when the Patriarch subdued the Ghost Kings of the Six Heavens and the Five Divisional Ghost Marshals, dispersing the malevolent and expelling the toxic. These were not the yin spirits of the dead. Now, the Patriarch has subjugated the Five Divisions and restored them to the correct path, thus consolidating the authority over pestilence. After swearing oaths to the Patriarch, the ghosts of the Five Divisions long ago returned to the true Dao. Thus, Zhang Yuanbo, through loyalty and sincerity, was appointed as the Direct Attendant of the Thunder Bureau. Zhao Gongming, through awe-inspiring integrity, became the Great General of the Dark Altar. The rest became chieftains of the grim prisons of Fengdu, no longer acting as demons.*

*In recent times, human hearts have grown perverse and deceitful, recklessly worshipping licentious shrines and inviting misfortune upon themselves. Ghosts arise from the mind, and illness stems from delusion. Thus, the demonic factions of the lower realms and the blood-consuming ghosts, receiving offerings, freely perpetrate their poisonous harm. This is not the doing of the Five Divisions after their subjugation, who would never again act recklessly.*

*The human heart is subtly wondrous, with qi and blood circulating throughout. The Three Regions and Eight Sceneries are all imbued with spirit within the true. Thus, one can repel the gods of life and death, becoming an Immortal of Great Sagehood. But if one deviates from proper nurturing, the Nine Orifices become obstructed, the body fails to generate spirit, and one becomes a walking corpse, a ghost borrowing qi, or a witless shade—far beyond the Five Pestilences alone.*

*Now, the Most High’s ancestral method for subduing the Six Heavens and Five Divisions is transmitted to suppress the Five Pestilences, decapitate demonic hordes, and purify the body of pestilential evil with talismans. Then, with the Celestial Talisman, one crushes the disease, and with upright qi, restores tranquility. This is called the Method for Saving the World and Subduing Pestilence.*

**Laojun’s Pestilence-Dispelling Celestial Talisman**
**Heavenly Master’s Pestilence-Expelling Talisman**

**Laojun’s Merciful Talisman for Co-Sleeping Without Contagion**
*The talisman’s form is fully revealed to sever pestilence and cut off plague.*

**Talisman for Inducing Sweat to Clear Pathways**
*See "Heavenly Heart, Marrow, Jade Maid, and the □□ Precious Chapters of the Dao and Virtue," Fourth Scroll.*

**Heavenly Master’s Great Petition to Sever Pestilence**
*The opening and closing of the petition follow the standard form, though the invoked officials differ. Here, their ranks and titles are specifically listed below.*

Respectfully petitioned for [Name], invoking the descent of:
— One hundred twenty Star Lords, officials, and functionaries,
— The Lord of the Ding Palace, charged with governance,
to seize and capture the plague-spirits within the domain, severing and annihilating all those that seek to spread contagion.

Further invoked are:
— Twelve Lords of the Nine Yi of the East,
— Twelve Lords of the Eight Man of the South,
— Twelve Lords of the Six Rong of the West,
— Twelve Lords of the Five Di of the North,
— Twelve Lords of the Three Qin of the Center,
with each of the Five Divisions commanding twelve hundred officers and three hundred thousand soldiers;
— Twenty-four Generals of the Three Household Guardians for [Name]’s city and residence,
along with thirty million officers and soldiers.

Together, they shall respond to this petition, descending upon the land within the domain, the sealed precincts, and the four directions and eight quarters, to resist, strike, and defend with strict encampment and protection, capturing and executing all.

Further invoked are the local earth gods of the altars of soil and grain—all the rightful deities customarily worshipped and entreated by the people for blessings—to join the aforementioned celestial officials and functionaries in unified effort, combining forces to guard and prepare, seizing and suppressing the plague-spirits that seek to harm the people of Heaven.

Above, the Celestial Net is unfurled to intercept and cover the flying malevolent spirits that bring affliction.
Below, the Earthly Snare is laid to permeate and purify the springs, sources, rivers, and waterways, as well as the hidden paths and concealed dens where harm is wrought upon humanity.

All shall be captured and driven out to the realm of the Underworld’s judgment.
The Yellow Slaves and Seven Sons, the Yearly Lords of Disease, the Five Pestilential Spirits of the Five Directions—all shall be shattered, crushed, and scattered to the winds a myriad leagues away, forbidden from lurking in secret to spread poison and wrongfully harm the good people.

Thus shall the nation’s borders be at peace, serving as proof of efficacy.
*[The petition concludes in the standard form.]*
**Method of the Petition**

The Master says: Those who have not yet studied the arts cannot ascend in spirit to present themselves before the Emperor, for their mortal forms remain unrefined, their primordial spirits yoked to yin, and thus unable to ascend. They must first engage in visualization to seek communion.

Begin by summoning forth the divine officers and generals, pacing the *gang* in accordance with the method—its steps are recorded in the *Gang* Canon. First, visualize the *qi* of the five viscera, transforming it into the true essence of the Five Phases. Then assemble the jade chariot’s ritual procession, with banners of the sun and moon, within the lower Sea of *Qi*. Mounting a single strand of white *qi*, ascend alongside the officers and functionaries from the western pillar of Mount Kunlun, reaching the realm of the *Gang* Winds, the domain of the sun, moon, and stars. Do not yet ascend further; first pace the *gang* to break through the *Gang* Winds—its steps are found in the *Gang* Canon.

Emerging from the *Gang* Winds, enter the Desire Realm. Tread upon the Nine Spirits to ascend into the Form Realm. Within both the Desire and Form Realms, all appears as the grandeur of earthly officials and wealthy households, yet no structures or traces of buildings are visible—one must perceive this with the heart and awaken to it inwardly. In the Form Realm, the Five Colors surge and billow, *qi* congealing into palaces, though these bear no resemblance to earthly architecture.

Next, pace the *gang* of the Three Realms in their subtle state to reach the Formless Realm. Here, one sees only golden light filling the space before them, with no sound or form to be heard. Beyond lies the realm of the Seed People, a domain of emptiness and Brahmanic *qi*. Riding this Brahmanic *qi*, ascend to the Great Clarity, where vast golden light radiates in all directions—soundless, formless. Within this golden light, the ancestral master appears to bestow the petition.

In an instant, the light parts, and the sage sits within a white radiance, though no words are spoken. Then present this plea: *"The celestial light dazzles me; my mortal nature cannot ascend further. I humbly beseech you to manifest in accordance with the private intentions of lesser practitioners, that I may receive the imperial decree."* At once, the white light transforms into a chamber—roofless, without beams or tiles, stepless, without stairs or platforms—seeming both present and absent, existent and non-existent. Entering this hall is called "ascending the hall." The appearance of red light is an auspicious omen.

Next, the Jade Hall remains unseen, and as before, golden light fills the space ahead. Following the path of heaven, descend and return to the altar. There, command the summoned officers and generals to capture the pestilential spirits, and so forth.

I, by the Emperor’s decree, assist in the transformations of heaven, aiding the state and saving the people. Now, in the domain of [so-and-so], pestilence spreads unchecked, and peace has not been restored. I have ascended in spirit to the Jade Palace, reverently received the imperial decree, and come to this place. Hearken with utmost sincerity:

The decree resounds: *Oṃ hūṃ hūṃ.*

The assembled deities bow their heads in reverence; evil demons return to rightness. Should any dare act with malice, they shall be reduced to dust. Hasten, hasten—upon receipt of this decree, act without delay.

The proclamation complete, you must swiftly obey the imperial command: expel the poisonous *qi* with all haste, driving it from this barren land. Should any disobey, they shall be bound by the *Ghost Statutes of the Yongshou Era*, and the pestilence-expelling talismans shall be burned to banish them beyond the four seas. Proceed as prescribed.

**Lao Jun’s Talisman for Pacifying the Household and Warding Off Pestilence**
*East, South, West, North, Upon the Bed, Above the Hearth, Rear-Facing Chamber*

For each talisman, recite this incantation and inscribe the Three Lights as prescribed:
*"I entrust myself to the midst of the Three Lights, within the Dipper’s bowl. A thousand ghosts and ten thousand spirits become my servants; all perverse essences under heaven submit and perish. Swiftly, swiftly—seize, transform, heal, heal! As urgent as an oral command."*

**The Northern Emperor’s Mudra and the *Qi* of the Three Lights**

**Method for Treating Consumptive Wasting**
The master says: Consumptive wasting arises when the heart is afflicted, causing *qi* to congeal and blood to stagnate. That it manifests as worms is due to wine and lust, immoderate diet, sorrow and joy, grief and chaos—all gradually leading to this state.

When worms form, it is because blood has congealed and *qi* has taken advantage. The *qi* that nourishes blood, when in the womb, is upright *qi*; when in the center, it forms accumulations; when it congeals in the heart’s domain, it becomes worms—all stemming from a heart not kept upright, and the karmic conditions of worry and thought.

The harm caused by the Three Corpses and Nine Worms must be understood in detail. Among the Nine Worms, six are transmitted across six generations, while three are not—such as the stomach’s *cunbai* worm. Some arise from toxins concentrated in the five viscera, or from habitual exposure within a family.

At the onset of transmission, one feels spirit and energy unsettled, no longer under one’s control, with vexation in the five centers, night sweats from the heart and kidneys, and palpitations. After ten days, the bones suddenly waste away, the face takes on a lustrous sheen, and the symptoms are confirmed.

The six worms, roughly every ten days, traverse the four limbs in cycles. The disease’s course depends on the *qi*’s generation: after the Beginning of Spring, they begin feeding, consuming for three days, then retreating for five. When they act, the body feels their bite; when they retreat, they return to their lair, drunk and dormant for five days, during which the illness temporarily subsides.

Only during their drunken retreat may talismans and medicines be administered; otherwise, the worms resist the power of the remedies, and the condition becomes untreatable.

A single worm occupies twelve limbs; six worms occupy seventy-two. In a month’s time: the first ten days, from the heart to the head, they roam the four limbs; the next ten, from the heart to the navel, they roam the four limbs; the last ten, from the navel to the feet, they roam the four limbs. When administering medicine or moxibustion, this must be carefully considered.

The master further says: To treat consumptive wasting, one must first understand the movement of toxic *qi* and upright *qi*. When congealed in the viscera, they form worms—male if encountered on a yang day, female on a yin day.

They first consume human fat, appearing white. Once the five viscera and six bowels are damaged, the skin wrinkles and hair falls out; in women, the blood ceases to flow. When the blood vessels are all harmed, they cannot nourish the five viscera and six bowels.

After seventy days, they consume human flesh and blood, turning yellow-red, damaging the muscles—hence emaciation, weakness, and inability to eat. The skin and sinews slacken, unable to contract.

After two hundred ten days, when flesh and blood are exhausted, they consume the marrow, turning black. When the marrow is eaten, the bones wither, and the patient cannot rise from bed.

Long-standing worms grow hair, their colors motley. They absorb the *qi* of the five viscera and five phases, and after being transmitted to three people, they mature, taking the form of birds. If they enter the kidney meridian, the condition becomes incurable.

The methods recorded here serve to instruct future generations. Thus, the classics say: If treated within sixty days, seven or eight out of ten may recover.

Within one hundred eighty days, if treated, three or four out of ten may recover; beyond this point, survival is rare. Here, the methods transmitted through six generations are recorded with care.

**First Generation:** Refers to the onset of illness, marked by sudden and unusual sensations. The worms resemble infants, all covered in long hair, or take the form of ghosts, or toads—varying in size. They disturb the patient’s soul and dreams, inverting day and night, scattering the *hun* and *po* spirits, dispersing vitality. Appetite wanes, the body aches, and such symptoms manifest. The worms become active on *bing*-*ding* days, targeting the heart during drunken sleep, affecting the four *shu* points.

**Second Generation:** Refers to the transmission of consumptive phlegm. The worms resemble tangled silk, about three *cun* long, or house lizards, centipedes, or shrimp. They induce a perpetual stupor, visions of the deceased at night, and joyful yet spirit-draining dreams. The chest feels full and oppressed, weakness and confusion deepen, and spontaneous sweating with fever arises. Such symptoms appear. The worms become active on *geng*-*xin* days, targeting the lungs during drunken sleep, affecting the four *shu* points.

**Third Generation:** Refers to the patient’s awareness of the illness, compounded by sorrow, allowing the *qi* to grow and reach the original viscera. As the heart stirs, *qi* descends; sorrow pertains to the kidney meridian. The worms resemble ant or mosquito larvae, clotted blood fragments, turtles, cicada shells, or dragonflies. They cause the *sanjiao* to grow clouded, inducing constant drowsiness, vomiting of bitter fluid, clear water, or sticky phlegm. Sores appear in the mouth and nose, lips blacken, the face turns ashen, the spirit wanders, the voice grows hoarse and dry, oily sweat flows, and the eyes dim with excessive tears. Such symptoms manifest. The worms become active on *gengyin* days, targeting the *jueyin* during drunken sleep, affecting the four *shu* points.

**Fourth Generation:** Refers to the worms having ravaged the lungs and depleted the heart, shifting to the spleen. The worms resemble tangled silk, lung tissue, or snakes. They cause phlegm accumulations in the intestines, alternating chills and fever, abdominal distension with visible veins, a faint wheezing cough that cannot cease, belching, bitter taste, or cravings for unusual foods. Such symptoms manifest. The worms become active on *wu*-*ji* days, targeting the spleen during drunken sleep, affecting the four *shu* points.

**Fifth Generation:** Refers to the patient’s illness worsening with anger and advancing *qi*. The worms resemble mice, or small jars—unformed and without clear boundaries—some with heads but no feet, others with feet but no heads, or resembling fragments of seminal essence. The three worms enter the lung meridian and settle in the kidneys, transforming upon encountering blood. The condition becomes unbearable, leaving the patient utterly debilitated, limbs slack, and incapable of any exertion. Some retain a ruddy complexion as in health, while others gain foresight, speaking of future events. Such symptoms manifest. The worms become active on *guiwei* days, targeting the liver during sleep, affecting the four *shu* points.

**Sixth Generation:** The worms may resemble horses with two tails, said to be male and female, or turtles, rotting silk, varying in length, or flying creatures with complete wings and feet, capable of transmitting *zhu* over a thousand *li*. *Zhu* refers to the so-called "flying corpse." This is no ordinary affliction; the method must be applied with discernment.

**Seals for Instruction:**
- *Seal of the Master’s Personal Verification to Eliminate Corpse-Worms*
- *Seal for Inquiring into Consumption*
- *Seal Matching the Form*

**Matching the Form**

The *Three Luminaries’ Fundamental Method* prescribes the structure for crafting talismans in *Matching the Form*. When preparing to administer a talisman to extract worms, first employ the *Talisman for Calming the Spirit and Securing Qi*, recite the *Incantation to Command the Essence-Soul*, and thereby stabilize the patient’s qi.

The incantation reads:
*Three Corpses bring calamity,*
*Nine Worms wreak havoc.*
*They devour the five viscera,*
*Flee to the bladder.*
*Be they crimson or white,*
*Azure or yellow,*
*Swallow this talisman into the belly,*
*Scour the stomach, purge the intestines.*
*Uphold against the hundred ailments,*
*Strengthen bones and joints.*
*Triple Burner, Four Seas,*
*Five viscera, six bowels—*
*At the talisman’s arrival, gather and harvest,*
*Dare they not perish?*
*Hasten, hasten, as decreed by law!*

Next, form the *Dipper Mudra* and recite the *Incantation of Heaven Round and Earth Square*, visualizing the *Six Ding Spirits*, *Three Generals*, *Twenty-Eight Constellations*, and *Eleven Luminaries* within the talisman brush. Then inscribe the talisman, envisioning flames issuing from the brush. Upon completion, deliver it to the patient to consume with peach broth.

First, invoke:
*Most High Lord Lao,*
*Teach me to slay demons.*
*Grant me divine formulas,*
*Instruct me to save the world,*
*Attach and extinguish disasters.*
*Inscribe talismans to cure illness,*
*Transmitting light across ten thousand li.*
*Spirits and gods submit,*
*Beings and people find peace.*
*Hasten, hasten, as decreed by law!*

Then recite:
*Shatter their form,*
*Recall the soul to the body,*
*Seven po settle in tranquility.*
*Guard the body, dispel illness,*
*Forever preserve longevity.*
*All spirits, awe-inspired,*
*At this command, obey and act.*

**Method for Discerning Treatable and Untreatable Cases**
The Master states: In cases of *corpse-transmission*, some are treatable, while others, where the disease has deeply advanced, the malevolent worms seize the true qi, the patient falls silent in self-seclusion, blood and qi are exhausted, are beyond remedy. To test this, take a bowl of water, silently draw in the patient’s *natal star qi*, recite the *Heavenly Peng Incantation*, and blow into the water, visualizing the natal star. Grasp the *Heavenly Peng Seal and Incantation*, point at the water, and envision yourself as the Heavenly Peng. Have the patient gaze into the water—if black qi appears, it is a demonic affliction. If they refuse to look or demand the water to inspect themselves, the case is untreatable.

Further verification lies in the brows’ markings, which foretell life or death. If the brow’s roots are dark or black, the eyes often gaze upward, and upon turning, black lines appear between the brows with qi like threads; if the brow’s corners bear azure qi, the brows are largely fallen, the brows are low while the brow’s roots are high, or hidden qi stirs restlessly between the brows, or the skin twitches intermittently—all such signs are untreatable.

This method is difficult to convey in writing or speech; it resides in the heart’s comprehension. Those who can pivot and adapt may grasp it through insight.

To identify worms when their color and qi remain unclear, employ the *Inquiry Talisman*. Craft the talisman according to the lunar phase, grinding cinnabar in alignment with the month’s stem, and inscribe it accordingly. Have the patient swallow it with frankincense broth. After the time it takes to eat a meal, have them hold frankincense up to the sun, shielding their eyes with their hands. If hair emerges from all ten fingertips, the disease is severe; if it appears from the middle fingers, the affliction runs deep. White hair indicates treatability, while yellow or red suggests difficulty. Absence of hair or sparse hair signifies no worms.

**Sequence for Pursuing Worms**
For those in the initial stages of transmission, when pursuing worms, one must first submit a memorial to the Supreme Emperor, the City God of Mount Tai, the local earth deities, and the officers and soldiers of the community, as well as the spirits of the deceased, before proceeding. Masters who have ascended in rank and entered the hall may act at will without hesitation.

First, have the patient swallow the *Three Luminaries Talisman* to weaken the malevolent qi. Then administer the talisman—none will fail to strike true. As evening approaches, have the patient consume the talisman and sit in their natal position (e.g., those born in the *zi* hour sit in the *zi* position), envisioning the Dipper’s light enveloping them. During the quiet of night, ensure lamps burn brightly before and behind, and prepare a wok of boiling oil. Do not allow the patient to leave, nor engage in conversation; only three to five people should keep watch. Soon, the patient may seem to dream of ghostly entities taking leave—ask their names. The worms may emerge from the patient’s body, clothing, or seat. Their forms vary; any creature with a discernible shape should be swiftly seized and cast into the boiling oil. Once fried, discard both the worms and the vessel into a flowing river, and depart without looking back.

**Incantation to the Patient While Administering Talisman**
*Nine Heavens’ Emperor,*
*Four Numinous Ones, Eight Gates.*

Recite again:

*Together cultivate the seven virtues.*

**Method for Hastening Birth and Resolving Childbirth Calamities**
The Master states: The mother receives the embryo through love and desire; the child takes form through karmic affinity. Without the mother, the child cannot be born; without the father, the mother cannot bestow life; without the child’s attachment to love and karma, it cannot acquire a body. Thus, causes and conditions give rise to karmic fruits and retributions.

The method for childbirth does not originate from the act of delivery. The child and mother unite qi to nurture form, and when the time comes to separate and be born, if the wind of past affections remains unsevered or the vitality of the destined birth is unknown, birth cannot occur.

Therefore, if the child and mother come through affection, the child is born easily, grows swiftly, and becomes intelligent. They attain wealth and nobility without toil, bringing honor to their parents. But if the child and mother come through enmity, there may be calamities of transverse or breech birth, or even the sorrow of stillbirth.

Next, if the child fails to grow to maturity, they may bring peril and distress to their kin—all of which arises from the excesses of *chongqian*. For those most afflicted by such transgressions, I now establish methods of salvation and remedy to safeguard life within the womb.

First, to protect the fetus and preserve vitality; then, to hasten delivery; and finally, to expedite birth—all follow a proper sequence. After birth, to ensure the child’s healthy growth, there are talismans to calm the heart, seals to secure the windows, methods to stimulate the appetite, soothe the soul, and treat fright—all detailed below, offered as benevolent remedies for the world.

**Talisman for Protecting the Fetus**
The Master says: When the fetal *qi* is weak or deficient, employ the **Three Lights Talisman**, prepared according to its prescribed method, to supplement and invigorate the generative *qi*.

**Talisman and Incantation for Safeguarding Life**
*"Preserve the spirit, pacify and secure,
Guard my bodily form.
The Spirit Lords of the Five Viscera,
Each ensure peace and tranquility."*

Draw the talisman by dipping the brush in *qi* of the Three Lights. First make the Dipper Mudra, then the Sun Deity Mudra, and again the Dipper Mudra before completing the talisman. Administer this during the first or second month of pregnancy.

*(Form combined)*
Inscribe this talisman with the *qi* of the dominant phase of the current month. Administer during the sixth or seventh month of pregnancy.
